🔐 Authentication Resources

Kubernetes authentication resources manage identity, access control, and security tokens for applications and services. In this section, we'll explore how to configure authentication for your anihpj Django application using ServiceAccounts - essential resources for securing pod-to-API communication.

📋 Authentication Resources Overview

ServiceAccount - Identity for pods and services
TokenRequest - Request authentication tokens
TokenReview - Validate authentication tokens
CertificateSigningRequest - Request and manage X.509 certificates

ServiceAccount

ServiceAccount Overview

ServiceAccountList - Collection of ServiceAccounts
Operations - API operations for management
Official Docs: ServiceAccount v1 API | API Version: v1

ServiceAccount binds together a name, authentication principal, and secrets for pod identity management.

Full Description

ServiceAccount provides an identity for processes that run in a Pod, enabling your anihpj Django application to authenticate with the Kubernetes API server. Each pod in your jobpost application can use a ServiceAccount to access cluster resources securely, making API calls, reading ConfigMaps, or accessing Secrets.

By default, Kubernetes automatically creates a default ServiceAccount in every namespace and mounts an API token into each pod. However, for production Django applications, you should create dedicated ServiceAccounts with minimal permissions following the principle of least privilege. This ensures your Skills, Author, Location, and JobPost services only have access to the resources they need.

Syntax

# Create a ServiceAccount from YAML file
kubectl create -f serviceaccount.yaml
# Create a ServiceAccount imperatively
kubectl create serviceaccount {name}
# List all ServiceAccounts
kubectl get serviceaccounts
# List all ServiceAccounts (short form)
kubectl get sa
# Get detailed information about a specific ServiceAccount
kubectl describe serviceaccount {name}
# Get detailed information about a specific ServiceAccount (short form)
kubectl describe sa {name}
# Get ServiceAccount in YAML format
kubectl get serviceaccount {name} -o yaml
# Delete a specific ServiceAccount
kubectl delete serviceaccount {name}
# Delete a specific ServiceAccount (short form)
kubectl delete sa {name}

YAML Structure

apiVersion: v1
kind: ServiceAccount
metadata:
  name: anihpj-django-sa
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: authentication
automountServiceAccountToken: true
imagePullSecrets:
- name: docker-registry-secret
secrets:
- name: anihpj-api-token

Parameters Description

  • apiVersion: string - API version, always "v1" for ServiceAccount
  • kind: string - Resource type, always "ServiceAccount"
  • metadata: ObjectMeta - Standard object metadata including name, namespace, labels, and annotations
  • automountServiceAccountToken: boolean - Whether pods using this ServiceAccount should automatically mount API tokens
  • imagePullSecrets: []LocalObjectReference - List of secrets for pulling container images
  • secrets: []ObjectReference - List of secrets that pods can use with this ServiceAccount

Return Value

  • 200 (ServiceAccount): OK - Request successful, ServiceAccount returned
  • 201 (ServiceAccount): Created - ServiceAccount successfully created
  • 202 (ServiceAccount): Accepted - Request accepted for processing
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Create ServiceAccount for Skills Model Service

This example demonstrates creating a dedicated ServiceAccount for the Skills model service in the jobpost app.

apiVersion: v1
kind: ServiceAccount
metadata:
  name: anihpj-skills-sa
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    model: skills
    component: api
automountServiceAccountToken: true
kubectl create -f skills-serviceaccount.yaml
serviceaccount/anihpj-skills-sa created
Example 2: Create ServiceAccount for User Authentication Service

This example shows creating a ServiceAccount for Django User model authentication with imagePullSecrets.

apiVersion: v1
kind: ServiceAccount
metadata:
  name: anihpj-user-sa
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    model: user
    component: auth
automountServiceAccountToken: true
imagePullSecrets:
- name: anihpj-registry-secret
kubectl create -f user-serviceaccount.yaml
kubectl describe sa anihpj-user-sa
serviceaccount/anihpj-user-sa created Name: anihpj-user-sa Namespace: default Labels: app=anihpj component=auth model=user Image pull secrets: anihpj-registry-secret Mountable secrets: Tokens:
Example 3: Create ServiceAccount for Author Content Service

This example illustrates creating a ServiceAccount for the Author model with specific secrets.

apiVersion: v1
kind: ServiceAccount
metadata:
  name: anihpj-author-sa
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    model: author
    component: content
automountServiceAccountToken: true
secrets:
- name: author-api-token
- name: author-db-credentials
kubectl create -f author-serviceaccount.yaml
kubectl get sa anihpj-author-sa -o yaml
serviceaccount/anihpj-author-sa created apiVersion: v1 kind: ServiceAccount metadata: name: anihpj-author-sa namespace: default labels: app: anihpj model: author component: content automountServiceAccountToken: true secrets: - name: author-api-token - name: author-db-credentials
Example 4: Create ServiceAccount for Location Lookup Service

This example demonstrates creating a ServiceAccount for the Location model geolocation service.

apiVersion: v1
kind: ServiceAccount
metadata:
  name: anihpj-location-sa
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    model: location
    component: geolocation
  annotations:
    description: "ServiceAccount for Location lookup and geolocation services"
automountServiceAccountToken: true
kubectl create -f location-serviceaccount.yaml
kubectl get sa -l model=location
serviceaccount/anihpj-location-sa created NAME SECRETS AGE anihpj-location-sa 0 5s
Example 5: Create ServiceAccount for JobPost API Service

This example shows creating a comprehensive ServiceAccount for the JobPost model API service with all security features.

apiVersion: v1
kind: ServiceAccount
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-sa
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    model: jobpost
    component: api
    environment: production
  annotations:
    description: "ServiceAccount for JobPost API with full permissions"
automountServiceAccountToken: true
imagePullSecrets:
- name: anihpj-registry-secret
- name: docker-hub-secret
secrets:
- name: jobpost-api-token
- name: jobpost-db-credentials
- name: jobpost-external-api-keys
kubectl create -f jobpost-serviceaccount.yaml
kubectl describe sa anihpj-jobpost-sa
serviceaccount/anihpj-jobpost-sa created Name: anihpj-jobpost-sa Namespace: default Labels: app=anihpj component=api environment=production model=jobpost Annotations: description: ServiceAccount for JobPost API with full permissions Image pull secrets: anihpj-registry-secret docker-hub-secret Mountable secrets: jobpost-api-token jobpost-db-credentials jobpost-external-api-keys Tokens:

ServiceAccountList

Official Docs: ServiceAccountList v1 API | API Version: v1

ServiceAccountList is a collection of ServiceAccount objects returned by list operations.

Full Description

ServiceAccountList represents a collection of ServiceAccounts in your Kubernetes cluster. When you query for multiple ServiceAccounts using kubectl or the Kubernetes API, the response is returned as a ServiceAccountList object. This is particularly useful for managing authentication across all services in your anihpj Django application, allowing you to view and manage ServiceAccounts for Skills, User, Author, Location, and JobPost models simultaneously.

Parameters Description

  • apiVersion: string - API version, always "v1"
  • kind: string - Resource type, always "ServiceAccountList"
  • metadata: ListMeta - Standard list metadata including resourceVersion and continue token
  • items: []ServiceAccount (required) - Array of ServiceAccount objects

Return Value

  • 200 (ServiceAccountList): OK - Request successful, list of ServiceAccounts returned
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required

5 Practical Django List Examples

Example 1: List All Skills Model ServiceAccounts

This example demonstrates listing all ServiceAccounts for the Skills model in the jobpost app.

# List all Skills ServiceAccounts
kubectl get serviceaccounts -l model=skills
NAME SECRETS AGE anihpj-skills-sa 0 5m anihpj-skills-ro-sa 0 3m anihpj-skills-rw-sa 0 2m
Example 2: List User Authentication ServiceAccounts with Details

This example shows listing User model ServiceAccounts with detailed output.

# List User ServiceAccounts with wide output
kubectl get sa -l model=user -o wide
NAME SECRETS AGE anihpj-user-sa 0 10m anihpj-user-admin 0 8m anihpj-user-api 0 5m
Example 3: List All Author Content ServiceAccounts in JSON

This example illustrates listing Author ServiceAccounts in JSON format for automation.

# List Author ServiceAccounts in JSON format
kubectl get serviceaccounts -l model=author -o json
{ "apiVersion": "v1", "kind": "ServiceAccountList", "items": [ { "metadata": { "name": "anihpj-author-sa", "namespace": "default", "labels": { "app": "anihpj", "model": "author" } }, "automountServiceAccountToken": true } ] }
Example 4: List Location ServiceAccounts Across Namespaces

This example demonstrates listing Location model ServiceAccounts across all namespaces.

# List Location ServiceAccounts in all namespaces
kubectl get sa -l model=location --all-namespaces
NAMESPACE NAME SECRETS AGE default anihpj-location-sa 0 15m production anihpj-location-sa 0 10m staging anihpj-location-sa 0 5m
Example 5: List All JobPost Application ServiceAccounts

This example shows listing all ServiceAccounts for the entire anihpj JobPost application.

# List all anihpj ServiceAccounts with sorting
kubectl get serviceaccounts -l app=anihpj --sort-by=.metadata.creationTimestamp
NAME SECRETS AGE anihpj-skills-sa 0 25m anihpj-user-sa 0 20m anihpj-author-sa 0 15m anihpj-location-sa 0 10m anihpj-jobpost-sa 0 5m

ServiceAccount Operations

Operations Overview

get - Read the specified ServiceAccount
list - List ServiceAccounts in namespace
list all - List ServiceAccounts in all namespaces
create - Create a ServiceAccount
update - Replace the specified ServiceAccount
patch - Partially update the specified ServiceAccount
delete - Delete a ServiceAccount
deletecollection - Delete collection of ServiceAccounts

Operations allow you to interact with ServiceAccount resources through the Kubernetes API. These operations enable you to manage authentication and authorization for your anihpj Django application pods, ensuring secure access to cluster resources.

get - read the specified ServiceAccount

Read details of a specific ServiceAccount by name.

HTTP Request
GET /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/serviceaccounts/{name}
Parameters
  • name (in path): string, required - name of the ServiceAccount
  • namespace (in path): string, required - namespace of the ServiceAccount
  • pretty (in query): string - pretty print output
Return Value
  • 200 (ServiceAccount): OK
  • 401: Unauthorized
5 Practical Django Examples
Example 1: Get Skills ServiceAccount Details

This example demonstrates retrieving details of the Skills model ServiceAccount.

# Get Skills ServiceAccount
kubectl get serviceaccount anihpj-skills-sa -o yaml
apiVersion: v1 kind: ServiceAccount metadata: name: anihpj-skills-sa namespace: default labels: app: anihpj model: skills automountServiceAccountToken: true
Example 2: Get User ServiceAccount with Secrets

This example shows retrieving User ServiceAccount with associated secrets.

# Get User ServiceAccount details
kubectl describe sa anihpj-user-sa
Name: anihpj-user-sa Namespace: default Labels: app=anihpj model=user Image pull secrets: anihpj-registry-secret Mountable secrets: Tokens: Events:
Example 3: Get Author ServiceAccount JSON

This example illustrates retrieving Author ServiceAccount in JSON format.

# Get Author ServiceAccount as JSON
kubectl get sa anihpj-author-sa -o json
{ "apiVersion": "v1", "kind": "ServiceAccount", "metadata": { "name": "anihpj-author-sa", "namespace": "default", "labels": { "app": "anihpj", "model": "author" } }, "automountServiceAccountToken": true, "secrets": [ {"name": "author-api-token"} ] }
Example 4: Get Location ServiceAccount Custom Columns

This example demonstrates retrieving Location ServiceAccount with custom columns.

# Get Location ServiceAccount with custom output
kubectl get sa anihpj-location-sa -o custom-columns=NAME:.metadata.name,NAMESPACE:.metadata.namespace,AGE:.metadata.creationTimestamp
NAME NAMESPACE AGE anihpj-location-sa default 2024-01-15T10:30:00Z
Example 5: Get JobPost ServiceAccount with Annotations

This example shows retrieving JobPost ServiceAccount including all annotations.

# Get JobPost ServiceAccount with annotations
kubectl get sa anihpj-jobpost-sa -o jsonpath='{.metadata.annotations}'
{"description":"ServiceAccount for JobPost API with full permissions"}

list - list or watch objects of kind ServiceAccount

List ServiceAccounts in a specific namespace with optional filtering and pagination.

HTTP Request
GET /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/serviceaccounts
Parameters
  • namespace (in path): string, required - namespace to list ServiceAccounts from
  • allowWatchBookmarks (in query): boolean - allow watch bookmarks
  • continue (in query): string - continue token for pagination
  • fieldSelector (in query): string - field selector to filter results
  • labelSelector (in query): string - label selector to filter results
  • limit (in query): integer - maximum number of results
  • pretty (in query): string - pretty print output
  • resourceVersion (in query): string - resource version
  • resourceVersionMatch (in query): string - how to match resource version
  • sendInitialEvents (in query): boolean - send initial events
  • timeoutSeconds (in query): integer - timeout in seconds
  • watch (in query): boolean - watch for changes
Return Value
  • 200 (ServiceAccountList): OK
  • 401: Unauthorized
5 Django Namespace List Examples
Example 1: List Skills ServiceAccounts in Default Namespace

This example demonstrates listing Skills model ServiceAccounts in default namespace.

This example shows watching JobPost ServiceAccounts for real-time changes.

NAME SECRETS AGE anihpj-jobpost-sa 0 30m anihpj-jobpost-sa 0 30m MODIFIED anihpj-jobpost-api 0 0s ADDED

list - list or watch objects of kind ServiceAccount (all namespaces)

List ServiceAccounts across all namespaces in the cluster.

HTTP Request
GET /api/v1/serviceaccounts
Parameters
  • allowWatchBookmarks (in query): boolean - allow watch bookmarks
  • continue (in query): string - continue token for pagination
  • fieldSelector (in query): string - field selector to filter results
  • labelSelector (in query): string - label selector to filter results
  • limit (in query): integer - maximum number of results
  • pretty (in query): string - pretty print output
  • resourceVersion (in query): string - resource version
  • resourceVersionMatch (in query): string - how to match resource version
  • sendInitialEvents (in query): boolean - send initial events
  • timeoutSeconds (in query): integer - timeout in seconds
  • watch (in query): boolean - watch for changes
Return Value
  • 200 (ServiceAccountList): OK
  • 401: Unauthorized

create - create a ServiceAccount

Create a new ServiceAccount in the specified namespace.

HTTP Request
POST /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/serviceaccounts
Parameters
  • namespace (in path): string, required - namespace to create ServiceAccount in
  • body: ServiceAccount, required - ServiceAccount object to create
  • dryRun (in query): string - dry run mode (All, None)
  • fieldManager (in query): string - name of the manager making changes
  • fieldValidation (in query): string - field validation mode (Strict, Warn, Ignore)
  • pretty (in query): string - pretty print output
Return Value
  • 200 (ServiceAccount): OK
  • 201 (ServiceAccount): Created
  • 202 (ServiceAccount): Accepted
  • 401: Unauthorized
5 Django Create Examples
Example 1: Create Skills ServiceAccount Imperatively

This example demonstrates creating a Skills ServiceAccount using kubectl create command.

# Create Skills ServiceAccount imperatively
kubectl create serviceaccount anihpj-skills-sa -n default
kubectl label sa anihpj-skills-sa app=anihpj model=skills
serviceaccount/anihpj-skills-sa created serviceaccount/anihpj-skills-sa labeled
Example 2: Create User ServiceAccount from YAML

This example shows creating User ServiceAccount from YAML manifest file.

apiVersion: v1
kind: ServiceAccount
metadata:
  name: anihpj-user-sa
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    model: user
automountServiceAccountToken: true
imagePullSecrets:
- name: docker-registry-secret
kubectl create -f user-serviceaccount.yaml
serviceaccount/anihpj-user-sa created
Example 3: Create Author ServiceAccount with Dry Run

This example illustrates creating Author ServiceAccount with dry run validation.

# Create with dry run
kubectl create serviceaccount anihpj-author-sa --dry-run=client -o yaml
# Apply the creation
kubectl create serviceaccount anihpj-author-sa
apiVersion: v1 kind: ServiceAccount metadata: name: anihpj-author-sa namespace: default serviceaccount/anihpj-author-sa created
Example 4: Create Location ServiceAccount with Annotations

This example demonstrates creating Location ServiceAccount with descriptive annotations.

# Create Location ServiceAccount with annotation
kubectl create sa anihpj-location-sa
kubectl annotate sa anihpj-location-sa description="ServiceAccount for Location geolocation service"
serviceaccount/anihpj-location-sa created serviceaccount/anihpj-location-sa annotated
Example 5: Create JobPost ServiceAccount with Full Configuration

This example shows creating comprehensive JobPost ServiceAccount with all options.

apiVersion: v1
kind: ServiceAccount
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-sa
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    model: jobpost
    environment: production
  annotations:
    description: "Production ServiceAccount for JobPost API"
automountServiceAccountToken: true
imagePullSecrets:
- name: anihpj-registry-secret
secrets:
- name: jobpost-api-token
kubectl create -f jobpost-serviceaccount.yaml
kubectl get sa anihpj-jobpost-sa
serviceaccount/anihpj-jobpost-sa created NAME SECRETS AGE anihpj-jobpost-sa 0 5s

update - replace the specified ServiceAccount

Replace an existing ServiceAccount with a new configuration.

HTTP Request
PUT /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/serviceaccounts/{name}
Parameters
  • name (in path): string, required - name of the ServiceAccount to update
  • namespace (in path): string, required - namespace of the ServiceAccount
  • body: ServiceAccount, required - updated ServiceAccount object
  • dryRun (in query): string - dry run mode (All, None)
  • fieldManager (in query): string - name of the manager making changes
  • fieldValidation (in query): string - field validation mode (Strict, Warn, Ignore)
  • pretty (in query): string - pretty print output
Return Value
  • 200 (ServiceAccount): OK
  • 201 (ServiceAccount): Created
  • 401: Unauthorized

Partially update a ServiceAccount without replacing the entire object.

HTTP Request
PATCH /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/serviceaccounts/{name}
Parameters
  • name (in path): string, required - name of the ServiceAccount to patch
  • namespace (in path): string, required - namespace of the ServiceAccount
  • body: Patch, required - patch data
  • dryRun (in query): string - dry run mode (All, None)
  • fieldManager (in query): string - name of the manager making changes
  • fieldValidation (in query): string - field validation mode (Strict, Warn, Ignore)
  • force (in query): boolean - force apply the patch
  • pretty (in query): string - pretty print output
Return Value
  • 200 (ServiceAccount): OK
  • 201 (ServiceAccount): Created
  • 401: Unauthorized

TokenRequest

TokenRequest Overview

TokenRequestSpec - Specification for token request
TokenRequestStatus - Status of token request
Operations - API operations for token creation
Official Docs: TokenRequest v1 API | API Version: authentication.k8s.io/v1

TokenRequest requests a token for a given service account, enabling secure authentication for Django applications.

Full Description

TokenRequest provides a mechanism to request authentication tokens for ServiceAccounts in your anihpj Django application. This resource is essential for implementing secure pod-to-API communication, allowing your Django services to authenticate with the Kubernetes API server or other services that require token-based authentication. TokenRequest creates temporary, scoped tokens that can be bound to specific objects and have configurable expiration times.

In the context of the anihpj Django application, TokenRequest enables secure communication between your jobpost services, user management components, and external APIs. The token mechanism ensures that only authorized pods can access sensitive resources, making it ideal for microservices architectures where different Django components need to authenticate with each other or with external services.

Syntax

# Create a token for a ServiceAccount
kubectl create token <serviceaccount-name>

# Create a token with specific audience
kubectl create token <serviceaccount-name> --audience=<audience>

# Create a token with expiration time
kubectl create token <serviceaccount-name> --duration=<duration>

# Create a token bound to a specific pod
kubectl create token <serviceaccount-name> --bound-object-kind=Pod --bound-object-name=<pod-name>

YAML Structure

apiVersion: authentication.k8s.io/v1
kind: TokenRequest
metadata:
  name: anihpj-token-request
  namespace: anihpj-prod
spec:
  audiences:
    - "https://kubernetes.default.svc"
    - "https://anihpj-api.example.com"
  expirationSeconds: 3600
  boundObjectRef:
    kind: Pod
    name: anihpj-jobpost-pod
    uid: "12345678-1234-1234-1234-123456789abc"

Parameters Description

  • audiences - Array of intended audiences for the token, must include identifiers that recipients will validate against
  • expirationSeconds - Requested duration of token validity in seconds, actual duration may vary based on server policy
  • boundObjectRef - Reference to an object that the token will be bound to, token only valid while bound object exists
  • boundObjectRef.kind - Type of object to bind to, valid values are 'Pod' and 'Secret'
  • boundObjectRef.name - Name of the object to bind the token to
  • boundObjectRef.uid - Unique identifier of the bound object for additional security

Return Value

  • 200 OK - TokenRequest successfully created, returns token and expiration details
  • 201 Created - TokenRequest resource created successfully
  • 202 Accepted - TokenRequest accepted for processing
  • 401 Unauthorized - Authentication failed, invalid or missing credentials
  • 403 Forbidden - Authorization failed, insufficient permissions for ServiceAccount

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Create Token for JobPost API Access

This example creates a token for the JobPost service to access external APIs.

apiVersion: authentication.k8s.io/v1
kind: TokenRequest
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-token
  namespace: anihpj-prod
spec:
  audiences:
    - "https://kubernetes.default.svc"
    - "https://anihpj-jobpost-api.example.com"
  expirationSeconds: 3600
# Create token for JobPost ServiceAccount
kubectl create token anihpj-jobpost-sa --namespace=anihpj-prod --duration=1h

TokenRequestSpec

Official Docs: TokenRequestSpec API | API Version: authentication.k8s.io/v1

TokenRequestSpec contains client provided parameters of a token request for anihpj Django services.

Full Description

TokenRequestSpec defines the specification for requesting authentication tokens in your anihpj Django application. This specification allows you to configure the token's intended audiences, expiration time, and object binding for enhanced security. The spec ensures that tokens are created with the appropriate scope and lifetime for your Django microservices architecture.

In the anihpj context, TokenRequestSpec enables precise control over how your Django services authenticate with each other and external APIs. You can specify multiple audiences for cross-service communication, set appropriate expiration times for different security contexts, and bind tokens to specific pods for enhanced security in production deployments.

Syntax

spec:
  audiences:
    - "https://kubernetes.default.svc"
    - "https://anihpj-api.example.com"
  expirationSeconds: 3600
  boundObjectRef:
    kind: Pod
    name: anihpj-django-pod
    uid: "12345678-1234-1234-1234-123456789abc"

Parameters Description

  • audiences (required) - Array of intended audiences for the token, recipients must identify with these identifiers
  • expirationSeconds - Requested duration of validity in seconds, server may return different duration
  • boundObjectRef - Reference to object that token will be bound to, token valid only while object exists
  • boundObjectRef.kind - Kind of the referent, valid values are 'Pod' and 'Secret'
  • boundObjectRef.name - Name of the bound object for token validation
  • boundObjectRef.uid - UID of the referent for additional security verification

Return Value

  • 200 OK - TokenRequestSpec validated successfully
  • 201 Created - TokenRequestSpec applied and accepted
  • 400 Bad Request - Invalid TokenRequestSpec configuration
  • 401 Unauthorized - Authentication required for spec validation

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Basic Skills Service Token Spec

This example shows a basic TokenRequestSpec for the Skills model service.

spec:
  audiences:
    - "https://kubernetes.default.svc"
  expirationSeconds: 3600
# Apply Skills service token spec
kubectl apply -f skills-token-spec.yaml
tokenrequest.authentication.k8s.io/anihpj-skills-token created
Example 2: User Service Token with Multiple Audiences

This example creates a TokenRequestSpec for User service with multiple target audiences.

    - "https://kubernetes.default.svc"
    - "https://anihpj-user-api.example.com"
    - "https://auth.example.com"
  expirationSeconds: 1800
# Create User service token with multiple audiences
kubectl create -f user-multi-audience-token.yaml

spec:
  audiences:
    - "https://anihpj-jobpost-api.example.com"
  expirationSeconds: 7200
  boundObjectRef:
    kind: Secret
    name: jobpost-api-credentials
    uid: "xyz98765-4321-8765-2109-abc987654321"
# Apply JobPost service secret-bound token spec
kubectl apply -f jobpost-secret-bound-token.yaml
tokenrequest.authentication.k8s.io/anihpj-jobpost-secret-bound created

TokenRequestStatus

Official Docs: TokenRequestStatus API | API Version: authentication.k8s.io/v1

TokenRequestStatus contains the result of a token request, including the generated token and expiration details.

Full Description

TokenRequestStatus represents the server response to a token request in your anihpj Django application. This status contains the actual bearer token that can be used for authentication, along with the expiration timestamp that indicates when the token will become invalid. The status is populated by the Kubernetes API server after successful token generation.

For anihpj Django services, TokenRequestStatus provides the authentication credentials needed for secure inter-service communication. The returned token can be used in HTTP Authorization headers when making requests to other Django services or external APIs that validate Kubernetes service account tokens.

Syntax

status:
  expirationTimestamp: "2024-11-02T15:30:00Z"
  token: "eyJhbGciOiJSUzI1NiIsImtpZCI6IjEyMzQ1Njc4LTEyMzQtMTIzNC0xMjM0LTEyMzQ1Njc4OTBhYiJ9..."

Parameters Description

  • expirationTimestamp (required) - Time when the returned token will expire, in RFC3339 format
  • token (required) - Opaque bearer token for authentication, JWT format containing service account information

Return Value

  • 200 OK - TokenRequestStatus retrieved successfully
  • 201 Created - Token generated and status populated
  • 401 Unauthorized - Authentication failed, cannot generate token
  • 403 Forbidden - Insufficient permissions for token generation

5 Practical Django Examples

TokenRequest Operations

Operations Overview

create - Create token of a ServiceAccount

TokenRequest operations allow you to create authentication tokens for ServiceAccounts in your anihpj Django application. These operations enable secure communication between Django microservices and external APIs by providing temporary, scoped authentication credentials.

create create token of a ServiceAccount

HTTP Method: POST | Endpoint: /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/serviceaccounts/{name}/token

Creates a new authentication token for the specified ServiceAccount in your anihpj Django application. This operation generates a temporary bearer token that can be used for API authentication.

Parameters
  • name (path) - Name of the TokenRequest resource
  • namespace (path) - Namespace where the ServiceAccount exists
  • body - TokenRequest object containing spec with audiences, expiration, and binding
  • dryRun (query) - Dry run mode, if present must be "All"
  • fieldManager (query) - Name of field manager for server-side apply
  • fieldValidation (query) - Field validation mode (Strict, Warn, Ignore)
  • pretty (query) - Pretty print output if present
Response Codes
  • 200 OK - Token created successfully, returns TokenRequest with status
  • 201 Created - TokenRequest resource created successfully
  • 202 Accepted - Request accepted for processing
  • 401 Unauthorized - Authentication failed or invalid credentials
  • 403 Forbidden - Insufficient permissions for ServiceAccount
Example Request
# Create token for JobPost ServiceAccount
curl -X POST \
  https://kubernetes.default.svc/api/v1/namespaces/anihpj-prod/serviceaccounts/anihpj-jobpost-sa/token \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer $KUBE_TOKEN" \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -d '{
    "apiVersion": "authentication.k8s.io/v1",
    "kind": "TokenRequest",
    "spec": {
      "audiences": ["https://anihpj-api.example.com"],
      "expirationSeconds": 3600
    }
  }'

TokenReview

Official Docs: TokenReview API | API Version: authentication.k8s.io/v1

TokenReview attempts to authenticate a token to a known user.

📋 TokenReview Overview

TokenReviewSpec - Specification for token validation
TokenReviewStatus - Result of token validation
Operations - API operations for token validation

✨ Enhanced Documentation: This guide features professional syntax highlighting powered by Prism.js, matching the quality of industry-standard documentation. All examples use your exact Django models with realistic outputs.

Full Description

TokenReview attempts to authenticate a token to a known user in your anihpj Django application. This resource enables the API server to verify bearer tokens by examining their validity, extracting user information, and determining associated permissions. TokenReview requests may be cached by the webhook token authenticator plugin in the kube-apiserver for improved performance.

For anihpj Django services, TokenReview provides a standardized way to validate JWT tokens, service account tokens, and other authentication credentials. The resource accepts a token in its spec and returns detailed information about the token's validity, the authenticated user or service account, and any associated groups or roles that can be used for authorization decisions in your Django microservices architecture.

Syntax

# Create TokenReview to validate authentication token
kubectl create -f - <<'EOF'
apiVersion: authentication.k8s.io/v1
kind: TokenReview
metadata:
  name: anihpj-token-validation
spec:
  token: "eyJhbGciOiJSUzI1NiIsImtpZCI6InNraWxsc19rZXkiLCJ0eXAiOiJKV1QifQ..."
EOF

# Validate token for specific audience
kubectl apply -f tokenreview-skills.yaml

# Check TokenReview validation result
kubectl get tokenreview anihpj-token-validation -o yaml

Parameters Description

  • metadata (ObjectMeta) - Standard object's metadata. More info: https://git.k8s.io/community/contributors/devel/sig-architecture/api-conventions.md#metadata
  • spec (TokenReviewSpec) - Required. Spec holds information about the request being evaluated
  • status (TokenReviewStatus) - Status is filled in by the server and indicates whether the request can be authenticated

Return Value

  • 200 (TokenReview) - OK
  • 201 (TokenReview) - Created
  • 202 (TokenReview) - Accepted
  • 401 - Unauthorized

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Skills Service Token Validation

Validate Skills service authentication token.

apiVersion: authentication.k8s.io/v1
kind: TokenReview
metadata:
  name: skills-token-review
spec:
  token: "eyJhbGciOiJSUzI1NiIsImtpZCI6InNraWxsc19rZXkifQ..."
  audiences:
    - "https://anihpj-skills-api.example.com"
# Create TokenReview for Skills service
kubectl apply -f skills-token-review.yaml
tokenreview.authentication.k8s.io/skills-token-review created
Example 2: User Service Token Validation

  audiences:
    - "https://anihpj-user-api.example.com"
    - "https://anihpj-auth-api.example.com"

TokenReviewSpec

Official Docs: TokenReviewSpec API | API Version: authentication.k8s.io/v1

TokenReviewSpec is a description of the token authentication request.

Full Description

TokenReviewSpec defines the specification for token validation requests in your anihpj Django application. It contains the bearer token that needs to be validated and optional audience constraints that limit which services or APIs the token should be valid for.

For anihpj Django services, TokenReviewSpec enables you to validate JWT tokens, service account tokens, and other authentication credentials by specifying the token string and the expected audiences.

Syntax

# Create TokenReview with spec for Skills service
kubectl apply -f skills-tokenreview.yaml

# Validate token with audiences
kubectl create -f user-tokenreview.yaml

Parameters Description

  • audiences ([]string) - List of identifiers that the resource server presented with the token identifies as. Audience-aware token authenticators will verify that the token was intended for at least one of the audiences in this list. If no audiences are provided, the audience will default to the audience of the Kubernetes apiserver.
  • token (string) - Token is the opaque bearer token.

Return Value

  • 200 OK - TokenReviewSpec processed successfully
  • 400 Bad Request - Invalid token format or missing required fields
  • 401 Unauthorized - Token validation failed

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Skills Service Token Spec

Basic TokenReviewSpec for Skills service validation.

spec:
  token: "eyJhbGciOiJSUzI1NiIsImtpZCI6InNraWxsc19rZXkifQ..."
  audiences:
    - "https://anihpj-skills-api.example.com"
# Apply Skills token review
kubectl apply -f skills-tokenreview.yaml
tokenreview.authentication.k8s.io/skills-tokenreview created
Example 2: User Service Multi-Audience Spec

TokenReviewSpec with multiple audiences for User service.

    - "https://anihpj-auth-api.example.com"
# Apply User token review

tokenreview.authentication.k8s.io/user-tokenreview created

TokenReviewStatus

Official Docs: TokenReviewStatus API | API Version: authentication.k8s.io/v1

TokenReviewStatus is the result of the token authentication request.

Full Description

TokenReviewStatus represents the server's response to a token validation request in your anihpj Django application. It contains information about whether the token is valid, the authenticated user or service account identity, associated groups, and the audiences for which the token is valid.

For anihpj Django services, TokenReviewStatus provides essential authentication information that can be used for authorization decisions in your Django microservices architecture.

Syntax

# Check TokenReviewStatus for validated token
kubectl get tokenreview skills-tokenreview -o yaml

# Extract authentication status
kubectl get tokenreview user-tokenreview -o jsonpath='{.status.authenticated}'

# Get user information
kubectl get tokenreview author-tokenreview -o jsonpath='{.status.user.username}'

Parameters Description

  • audiences ([]string) - Audience identifiers chosen by the authenticator that are compatible with both the TokenReview and token
  • authenticated (boolean) - Authenticated indicates that the token was associated with a known user
  • error (string) - Error indicates that the token couldn't be checked
  • user (UserInfo) - User is the UserInfo associated with the provided token

Return Value

  • 200 OK - TokenReviewStatus retrieved successfully
  • 401 Unauthorized - Token validation failed
  • 403 Forbidden - Access denied to validation results
  • 404 Not Found - TokenReview resource not found

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Skills Service Token Status

Successful TokenReviewStatus for Skills service.

status:
  authenticated: true
  user:
    username: "system:serviceaccount:anihpj:skills-sa"
    uid: "12345678-1234-5678-9abc-123456789abc"
    groups:
      - "system:serviceaccounts"
      - "system:serviceaccounts:anihpj"
  audiences:
    - "https://anihpj-skills-api.example.com"
# Check Skills token status
kubectl get tokenreview skills-tokenreview -o yaml
authenticated: true
Example 2: User Service Multi-Audience Status

TokenReviewStatus for User service with multiple audiences.

  authenticated: true

      - "system:serviceaccounts"
      - "system:serviceaccounts:anihpj"
  audiences:
    - "https://anihpj-user-api.example.com"
    - "https://anihpj-auth-api.example.com"
# Check User token status

true

TokenReview Operations

Operations Overview

create - Create a TokenReview

TokenReview operations enable token validation functionality for your anihpj Django application. These operations allow you to validate authentication tokens and extract user information for authorization decisions.

create - create a TokenReview

Create a new TokenReview to validate authentication tokens for your anihpj Django application services.

HTTP Request
POST /apis/authentication.k8s.io/v1/tokenreviews
Parameters
  • body (in body): TokenReview, required - TokenReview object containing spec with token and optional audiences
  • dryRun (in query): string - When present, indicates that modifications should not be persisted
  • fieldManager (in query): string - fieldManager is a name associated with the actor or entity
  • fieldValidation (in query): string - fieldValidation instructs the server on how to handle objects
  • pretty (in query): string - If 'true', then the output is pretty printed
Return Value
  • 200 (TokenReview): OK - Token validation completed successfully
  • 201 (TokenReview): Created - TokenReview resource created and processed
  • 202 (TokenReview): Accepted - Request accepted for processing
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required
5 Practical Django Examples
Example 1: Validate Skills Service Token

This example demonstrates validating a Skills model service authentication token.

# Create TokenReview for Skills service token validation
kubectl create -f - <<'EOF'
apiVersion: authentication.k8s.io/v1
kind: TokenReview
metadata:
  name: skills-token-validation
spec:
  token: eyJhbGciOiJSUzI1NiIsImtpZCI6InNraWxsc19rZXkifQ...
  audiences:
    - https://anihpj-skills-api.example.com
EOF
tokenreview.authentication.k8s.io/skills-token-validation created status: authenticated: true user: username: system:serviceaccount:anihpj:skills-sa

CertificateSigningRequest

Official Docs: CertificateSigningRequest API | API Version: certificates.k8s.io/v1

CertificateSigningRequest objects provide a mechanism to obtain x509 certificates by submitting a certificate signing request and asynchronously receiving the signed certificate.

📋 CertificateSigningRequest Overview

CertificateSigningRequestSpec - Certificate request specification
CertificateSigningRequestStatus - Certificate request status
CertificateSigningRequestList - Collection of CertificateSigningRequests
Operations - API operations for certificate management

Full Description

CertificateSigningRequest provides a comprehensive X.509 certificate management system for your anihpj Django application services. This resource enables secure TLS communication between your Skills, User, Author, Location, and JobPost services by automating certificate request, approval, and lifecycle management workflows.

For anihpj Django microservices, CertificateSigningRequest handles client certificates for API authentication, server certificates for HTTPS endpoints, and kubelet certificates for node communication. The resource supports automated approval workflows, expiration management, and integration with your Django service authentication system.

Syntax

# Create CertificateSigningRequest for service authentication
kubectl create -f - <<'EOF'
apiVersion: certificates.k8s.io/v1
kind: CertificateSigningRequest
metadata:
  name: anihpj-service-csr
spec:
  request: LS0tLS1CRUdJTiBDRVJUSUZJQ0FURSBSRVFVRVNULS0tLS0K...
  signerName: kubernetes.io/kube-apiserver-client
  usages:
  - client auth
  - digital signature
EOF

# Approve certificate request
kubectl certificate approve anihpj-service-csr

# Check certificate status
kubectl get csr anihpj-service-csr -o yaml

Parameters Description

  • apiVersion: string - API version, always "certificates.k8s.io/v1"
  • kind: string - Resource type, always "CertificateSigningRequest"
  • metadata: ObjectMeta - Standard object metadata including name and labels
  • spec: CertificateSigningRequestSpec - Certificate request specification with CSR data and signer
  • status: CertificateSigningRequestStatus - Request status with conditions and issued certificate

Return Values

  • 200 (CertificateSigningRequest): Successful operation
  • 201 (CertificateSigningRequest): Created successfully
  • 401: Unauthorized access
  • 422: Validation failed

5 Django Examples

Example 1: Skills Service Client Certificate

Create client certificate for Skills service API authentication.

apiVersion: certificates.k8s.io/v1
kind: CertificateSigningRequest
metadata:
  name: anihpj-skills-client-csr
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    service: skills
    purpose: client-auth
spec:
  request: LS0tLS1CRUdJTiBDRVJUSUZJQ0FURSBSRVFVRVNULS0tLS0K...
  signerName: kubernetes.io/kube-apiserver-client
  usages:
  - client auth
  - digital signature
# Create Skills service client certificate request
kubectl apply -f skills-client-csr.yaml
certificatesigningrequest.certificates.k8s.io/anihpj-skills-client-csr created
Example 2: User Service Serving Certificate

    service: user

  usages:
  - server auth
  - digital signature
  - key encipherment

CertificateSigningRequestSpec

Official Docs: CertificateSigningRequestSpec API | API Version: certificates.k8s.io/v1

CertificateSigningRequestSpec contains the certificate request specification and is immutable after creation.

Full Description

CertificateSigningRequestSpec defines the certificate request details for your anihpj Django application services. This specification includes the actual certificate signing request, signer information, expiration settings, and key usage requirements essential for establishing secure TLS communication between your Skills, User, Author, Location, and JobPost services.

Syntax

spec:
  # Base64-encoded certificate signing request (CSR) in PEM format
  request: LS0tLS1CRUdJTiBDRVJUSUZJQ0FURSBSRVFVRVNULS0tLS0K...
  # Signer responsible for issuing the certificate
  signerName: kubernetes.io/kube-apiserver-client
  # Certificate expiration time in seconds (minimum 600 seconds)
  expirationSeconds: 86400
  # Key usages for the requested certificate
  usages:
  - client auth
  - digital signature

Parameters Description

  • request: []byte (required) - Base64-encoded X.509 certificate signing request in PEM format
  • signerName: string (required) - Qualified name of the certificate signer
  • expirationSeconds: int32 - Requested certificate validity duration in seconds (minimum 600)
  • usages: []string - Key usages for the certificate (client auth, server auth, digital signature, etc.)
  • username: string - User who created the request (populated by API server)
  • uid: string - UID of the user who created the request (populated by API server)
  • groups: []string - Group membership of the creating user (populated by API server)
  • extra: map[string][]string - Extra attributes of the creating user (populated by API server)

CertificateSigningRequestStatus

Official Docs: CertificateSigningRequestStatus API | API Version: certificates.k8s.io/v1

CertificateSigningRequestStatus contains conditions indicating approved/denied/failed status and the issued certificate.

Full Description

CertificateSigningRequestStatus provides real-time information about your anihpj Django application certificate requests. This status object tracks the approval state, issued certificates, and failure conditions for certificate requests from your Skills, User, Author, Location, and JobPost services, enabling automated certificate lifecycle management.

Syntax

status:
  certificate: LS0tLS1CRUdJTiBDRVJUSUZJQ0FURS0tLS0t...
  conditions:
  - type: Approved
    status: "True"
    reason: AutoApproved
    message: "Certificate request approved by anihpj-controller"
    lastUpdateTime: "2024-01-15T10:30:00Z"

Parameters Description

  • certificate: []byte - PEM-encoded issued certificate (set after approval)
  • conditions: []CertificateSigningRequestCondition - Current conditions (Approved, Denied, Failed)
  • conditions[].type: string - Condition type (Approved, Denied, Failed)
  • conditions[].status: string - Condition status (True, False, Unknown)
  • conditions[].reason: string - Brief reason for the condition
  • conditions[].message: string - Human-readable message with condition details
  • conditions[].lastUpdateTime: Time - Last condition update timestamp
  • conditions[].lastTransitionTime: Time - Last condition transition timestamp

5 Django Examples

Example 1: Skills Service Approved Status

This example demonstrates an approved CertificateSigningRequestStatus for Skills service.

status:
  certificate: LS0tLS1CRUdJTiBDRVJUSUZJQ0FURS0tLS0t...
  conditions:
  - type: Approved
    status: "True"
    reason: AutoApproved
    message: "Certificate request approved by anihpj-controller"
    lastUpdateTime: "2024-01-15T10:30:00Z"
Example 2: User Service Pending Status

This example shows a User service certificate request waiting for approval.

This example illustrates a denied certificate request for Author service.

This example demonstrates a failed certificate issuance for Location service.

    lastUpdateTime: "2024-01-15T10:15:00Z"

This example shows a JobPost service with multiple status conditions over time.

CertificateSigningRequestList

Official Docs: CertificateSigningRequestList API | API Version: certificates.k8s.io/v1

CertificateSigningRequestList is a collection of CertificateSigningRequest objects returned by list operations.

Full Description

CertificateSigningRequestList provides a comprehensive view of all certificate requests in your anihpj Django application cluster. This collection enables bulk operations, status monitoring, and administrative oversight of certificate lifecycle management across your Skills, User, Author, Location, and JobPost services.

Syntax

# List all CertificateSigningRequests
kubectl get csr

# List with labels
kubectl get csr -l app=anihpj

# List in JSON format
kubectl get csr -o json

Parameters Description

  • apiVersion: string - API version, always "certificates.k8s.io/v1"
  • kind: string - Resource type, always "CertificateSigningRequestList"
  • metadata: ListMeta - Standard list metadata including resource version
  • items: []CertificateSigningRequest - Array of CertificateSigningRequest objects

Operations

Operations Overview: Complete CertificateSigningRequest API operations for managing certificate lifecycle

All CertificateSigningRequest operations for managing certificate lifecycle in your anihpj Django application.

Operations Overview

get - Read the specified CertificateSigningRequest
get approval - Read approval of the specified CertificateSigningRequest
get status - Read status of the specified CertificateSigningRequest
list - List or watch objects of kind CertificateSigningRequest
create - Create a CertificateSigningRequest
update - Replace the specified CertificateSigningRequest
update approval - Replace approval of the specified CertificateSigningRequest
update status - Replace status of the specified CertificateSigningRequest
patch - Partially update the specified CertificateSigningRequest
patch approval - Partially update approval of the specified CertificateSigningRequest
patch status - Partially update status of the specified CertificateSigningRequest
delete - Delete a CertificateSigningRequest
deletecollection - Delete collection of CertificateSigningRequest

create - create a CertificateSigningRequest

Create a new CertificateSigningRequest to request X.509 certificates for your anihpj Django application services.

HTTP Request
POST /apis/certificates.k8s.io/v1/certificatesigningrequests
Parameters
  • body (in body): CertificateSigningRequest, required - CertificateSigningRequest object
  • dryRun (in query): string - When present, indicates that modifications should not be persisted
  • fieldManager (in query): string - FieldManager is a name associated with the actor or entity
  • fieldValidation (in query): string - FieldValidation instructs the server on how to handle objects
  • pretty (in query): string - If 'true', then the output is pretty printed
Return Value
  • 200 (CertificateSigningRequest): OK
  • 201 (CertificateSigningRequest): Created
  • 202 (CertificateSigningRequest): Accepted
  • 401: Unauthorized
5 Django Create Examples
Example 1: Create Skills Service Client Certificate Request

This example demonstrates creating a CertificateSigningRequest for the Skills model service client authentication.

# Create Skills service client certificate request
kubectl apply -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: certificates.k8s.io/v1
kind: CertificateSigningRequest
metadata:
  name: anihpj-skills-client-csr
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    service: skills
spec:
  request: $(cat skills-client.csr | base64 | tr -d '\n')
  signerName: kubernetes.io/kube-apiserver-client
  usages:
  - client auth
  - digital signature
EOF
certificatesigningrequest.certificates.k8s.io/anihpj-skills-client-csr created

  • 401: Unauthorized

list - list CertificateSigningRequests

List all CertificateSigningRequests in the cluster with optional filtering and sorting capabilities.

Parameters
  • labelSelector (in query): string - label selector to filter results

  • limit (in query): integer - maximum number of results
  • continue (in query): string - continue token for pagination
  • pretty (in query): string - pretty print output
Return Value
  • 200 (CertificateSigningRequestList): OK
  • 401: Unauthorized

LocalSubjectAccessReview

LocalSubjectAccessReview Overview

Operations - API operations for management
Official Docs: LocalSubjectAccessReview v1 API | API Version: authorization.k8s.io/v1

LocalSubjectAccessReview checks whether a user or ServiceAccount can perform an action in a specific namespace for namespace-level RBAC validation.

Full Description

LocalSubjectAccessReview provides a way to check if a subject (user or ServiceAccount) has permission to perform a specific action on a resource within a namespace. Unlike SubjectAccessReview which is cluster-scoped, LocalSubjectAccessReview is namespace-scoped and respects namespace-level RoleBindings.

This is particularly useful for managing authentication across all services in your anihpj Django application, allowing you to verify namespace-level permissions for Skills, User, Author, Location, and JobPost models before granting access. By testing permissions in advance, you can ensure proper RBAC configurations and prevent runtime authorization failures.

Key Features:

  • Namespace-Scoped Checks: Verifies permissions within a specific namespace context
  • RBAC Validation: Tests Role and RoleBinding configurations for services
  • Service Permission Auditing: Validates that anihpj services have correct namespace-level permissions
  • Security Testing: Confirms permission boundaries before granting access
  • Immediate Response: Returns permission check results without modifying any resources

Syntax

# Create a LocalSubjectAccessReview from YAML file
kubectl create -f localsubjectaccessreview.yaml
# Create a LocalSubjectAccessReview using raw API
kubectl create --raw /apis/authorization.k8s.io/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/localsubjectaccessreviews -f permission-check.json
# Check if current user can create pods in namespace
kubectl auth can-i create pods -n skills
# Check if ServiceAccount can perform action
kubectl auth can-i create deployments --as=system:serviceaccount:user:anihpj-user-sa -n user

YAML Structure

apiVersion: authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: LocalSubjectAccessReview

metadata:
  name: string
  namespace: string

spec:
  resourceAttributes:
    namespace: string
    verb: string
    group: string
    version: string
    resource: string
    subresource: string
    name: string
  nonResourceAttributes:
    path: string
    verb: string
  user: string
  groups:
    - string
  extra:
    key:
      - string
  uid: string

status:
  allowed: boolean
  denied: boolean
  reason: string
  evaluationError: string

Parameters Description

  • apiVersion: string - API version, always "authorization.k8s.io/v1" for LocalSubjectAccessReview
  • kind: string - Resource type, always "LocalSubjectAccessReview"
  • metadata: ObjectMeta - Standard object metadata. Must include namespace field for namespace-scoped checks
  • spec: SubjectAccessReviewSpec (required) - Specification of the permission check to perform
  • spec.resourceAttributes: ResourceAttributes - Attributes for resource-based permission checks (namespace, verb, group, version, resource, subresource, name)
  • spec.nonResourceAttributes: NonResourceAttributes - Attributes for non-resource URL checks (path, verb)
  • spec.user: string - User to check permissions for (omit to check current user)
  • spec.groups: []string - Groups the user belongs to
  • spec.extra: map[string][]string - Additional attributes
  • spec.uid: string - UID of the user
  • status: SubjectAccessReviewStatus - Result of the permission check (populated by API server)
  • status.allowed: boolean - True if the action is allowed
  • status.denied: boolean - True if explicitly denied by policy
  • status.reason: string - Human-readable reason for the decision
  • status.evaluationError: string - Error message if evaluation failed

Return Value

  • 200 (LocalSubjectAccessReview): OK - Request successful, permission check completed
  • 201 (LocalSubjectAccessReview): Created - Permission check successfully created
  • 202 (LocalSubjectAccessReview): Accepted - Request accepted for processing
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Check Skills Service Pod Creation Permission

This example demonstrates checking if the Skills service account can create pods in the skills namespace.

apiVersion: authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: LocalSubjectAccessReview
metadata:
  namespace: skills
spec:
  resourceAttributes:
    namespace: skills
    verb: create
    group: ""
    version: v1
    resource: pods
  user: system:serviceaccount:skills:anihpj-skills-sa
# Check Skills service pod creation permission
kubectl create -f skills-permission-check.yaml
localsubjectaccessreview.authorization.k8s.io/skills-permission-check created Status: allowed=true Reason: RBAC: allowed by RoleBinding 'skills-pod-creator' in namespace 'skills'
Example 2: Check User Service Deployment Update Permission

This example verifies if the User service can update deployments in the user namespace.

apiVersion: authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: LocalSubjectAccessReview
metadata:
  namespace: user
spec:
  resourceAttributes:
    namespace: user
    verb: update
    group: apps
    version: v1
    resource: deployments
    name: anihpj-user-api
  user: system:serviceaccount:user:anihpj-user-sa
# Check User service deployment update permission
kubectl create -f user-permission-check.yaml
kubectl describe localsubjectaccessreview -n user
localsubjectaccessreview.authorization.k8s.io/user-permission-check created Name: user-permission-check Namespace: user API Version: authorization.k8s.io/v1 Kind: LocalSubjectAccessReview Status: Allowed: true Reason: RBAC: allowed by RoleBinding 'user-deployment-manager' in namespace 'user'
Example 3: Check Author Service Secret Read Permission

This example checks if the Author service can read secrets in the author namespace.

apiVersion: authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: LocalSubjectAccessReview
metadata:
  namespace: author
spec:
  resourceAttributes:
    namespace: author
    verb: get
    group: ""
    version: v1
    resource: secrets
  user: system:serviceaccount:author:anihpj-author-sa
# Check Author service secret read permission
kubectl create -f author-permission-check.yaml -o yaml
apiVersion: authorization.k8s.io/v1 kind: LocalSubjectAccessReview metadata: namespace: author spec: resourceAttributes: namespace: author verb: get resource: secrets user: system:serviceaccount:author:anihpj-author-sa status: allowed: false denied: true reason: "RBAC: no Role or RoleBinding found in namespace 'author' for secret access"
Example 4: Check Location Service ConfigMap List Permission

This example verifies if the Location service can list ConfigMaps in the location namespace.

apiVersion: authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: LocalSubjectAccessReview
metadata:
  namespace: location
spec:
  resourceAttributes:
    namespace: location
    verb: list
    group: ""
    version: v1
    resource: configmaps
  user: system:serviceaccount:location:anihpj-location-sa
# Check Location service ConfigMap list permission
kubectl create -f location-permission-check.yaml
kubectl get localsubjectaccessreview -n location -o jsonpath='{.status}'
localsubjectaccessreview.authorization.k8s.io/location-permission-check created {"allowed":true,"reason":"RBAC: allowed by RoleBinding 'location-config-reader' in namespace 'location'"}
Example 5: Check JobPost Service StatefulSet Delete Permission

This example checks if the JobPost service can delete StatefulSets in the jobpost namespace.

apiVersion: authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: LocalSubjectAccessReview
metadata:
  namespace: jobpost
spec:
  resourceAttributes:
    namespace: jobpost
    verb: delete
    group: apps
    version: v1
    resource: statefulsets
    name: anihpj-jobpost-db
  user: system:serviceaccount:jobpost:anihpj-jobpost-sa
# Check JobPost service StatefulSet delete permission
kubectl create -f jobpost-permission-check.yaml
kubectl describe localsubjectaccessreview -n jobpost
localsubjectaccessreview.authorization.k8s.io/jobpost-permission-check created Name: jobpost-permission-check Namespace: jobpost API Version: authorization.k8s.io/v1 Kind: LocalSubjectAccessReview Status: Allowed: false Denied: true Reason: RBAC: user lacks delete permission on statefulsets in namespace 'jobpost'

LocalSubjectAccessReview Operations

Operations Overview

create - Create a LocalSubjectAccessReview

Operations allow you to interact with LocalSubjectAccessReview resources through the Kubernetes API. These operations enable you to validate namespace-level permissions for your anihpj Django application services, ensuring secure access to resources within specific namespaces.

create - create a LocalSubjectAccessReview

Create a LocalSubjectAccessReview to check if a subject can perform an action within a namespace.

HTTP Request
POST /apis/authorization.k8s.io/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/localsubjectaccessreviews
Parameters
  • namespace (in path): string, required - namespace to check permissions in
  • body: LocalSubjectAccessReview, required - the permission check specification
  • dryRun (in query): string - dry run mode
  • fieldManager (in query): string - field manager name
  • fieldValidation (in query): string - field validation policy (Strict, Warn, Ignore)
  • pretty (in query): string - pretty print output
Return Value
  • 200 (LocalSubjectAccessReview): OK
  • 201 (LocalSubjectAccessReview): Created
  • 202 (LocalSubjectAccessReview): Accepted
  • 401: Unauthorized
5 Practical Django Examples

This example demonstrates validating if Skills service can create Jobs for background processing.

  namespace: skills

  resourceAttributes:
    namespace: skills
    verb: create
    group: batch
    version: v1
    resource: jobs
  user: system:serviceaccount:skills:anihpj-skills-sa

# Verify User service PVC management permission

kubectl describe localsubjectaccessreview -n user
localsubjectaccessreview.authorization.k8s.io/user-pvc-permission created Name: user-pvc-permission Namespace: user Status: Allowed: true Reason: RBAC: allowed by RoleBinding 'user-pvc-manager'
Example 3: Check Author Service Service Watch Permission

This example illustrates checking if Author service can watch Service resources.

apiVersion: authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: LocalSubjectAccessReview
metadata:
  namespace: author
spec:
  resourceAttributes:
    namespace: author
    verb: watch
    group: ""
    version: v1
    resource: services
  user: system:serviceaccount:author:anihpj-author-sa
# Check Author service Service watch permission
kubectl create -f author-service-watch.yaml -o yaml
apiVersion: authorization.k8s.io/v1 kind: LocalSubjectAccessReview metadata: namespace: author status: allowed: false reason: "RBAC: watch permission not granted"
Example 4: Audit Location Service Event Creation Permission

This example demonstrates auditing whether Location service can create Events.

apiVersion: authorization.k8s.io/v1

  namespace: location

  resourceAttributes:
    namespace: location
    verb: create
    group: ""

    resource: events
  user: system:serviceaccount:location:anihpj-location-sa
# Audit Location service event creation permission

localsubjectaccessreview.authorization.k8s.io/location-event-permission created {"allowed":true,"reason":"RBAC: allowed by RoleBinding 'location-event-creator'"}
{ "kind": "LocalSubjectAccessReview", "apiVersion": "authorization.k8s.io/v1", "metadata": { "creationTimestamp": null }, "spec": { "resourceAttributes": { "namespace": "location", "verb": "create", "resource": "events" }, "user": "system:serviceaccount:location:anihpj-location-logger" }, "status": { "allowed": true, "reason": "RBAC: allowed by RoleBinding 'location-event-creator'" } }

SelfSubjectAccessReview

SelfSubjectAccessReview Overview

SelfSubjectAccessReviewSpec - Access request specification
Operations - API operations for management
Official Docs: SelfSubjectAccessReview v1 API | API Version: authorization.k8s.io/v1

SelfSubjectAccessReview checks whether the current user can perform an action, enabling self-service permission validation.

Full Description

SelfSubjectAccessReview provides a way for users to check their own permissions before attempting actions. Unlike SubjectAccessReview and LocalSubjectAccessReview which check permissions for other users, SelfSubjectAccessReview is specifically for the current authenticated user to validate their own access rights.

This is particularly useful for your anihpj Django application where services need to verify their own capabilities before performing operations. For example, the Skills, User, Author, Location, and JobPost services can check if they have permission to create, update, or delete resources without actually attempting the action. Not specifying a namespace means "in all namespaces," making it flexible for both cluster-wide and namespace-scoped checks.

Key Features:

  • Self-Permission Checks: Users validate their own permissions without admin privileges
  • Cluster-Wide or Namespace-Scoped: Check permissions across all namespaces or within specific ones
  • Pre-Action Validation: Verify access before attempting operations to prevent errors
  • Service Account Auditing: ServiceAccounts can check their own RBAC permissions
  • No Side Effects: Permission checks don't modify any resources or leave audit trails

Syntax

# Check if current user can create pods
kubectl auth can-i create pods
# Check if current user can delete deployments in specific namespace
kubectl auth can-i delete deployments -n skills
# Check if current user can list secrets cluster-wide
kubectl auth can-i list secrets --all-namespaces
# Create SelfSubjectAccessReview from YAML file
kubectl create -f selfsubjectaccessreview.yaml

YAML Structure

apiVersion: authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: SelfSubjectAccessReview

metadata:
  name: string

spec:
  resourceAttributes:
    namespace: string
    verb: string
    group: string
    version: string
    resource: string
    subresource: string
    name: string
  nonResourceAttributes:
    path: string
    verb: string

status:
  allowed: boolean
  denied: boolean
  reason: string
  evaluationError: string

Parameters Description

  • apiVersion: string - API version, always "authorization.k8s.io/v1" for SelfSubjectAccessReview
  • kind: string - Resource type, always "SelfSubjectAccessReview"
  • metadata: ObjectMeta - Standard object metadata
  • spec: SelfSubjectAccessReviewSpec (required) - Specification of the access request for the current user
  • spec.resourceAttributes: ResourceAttributes - Attributes for resource-based permission checks (namespace, verb, group, version, resource, subresource, name)
  • spec.nonResourceAttributes: NonResourceAttributes - Attributes for non-resource URL checks (path, verb)
  • status: SubjectAccessReviewStatus - Result of the permission check (populated by API server)
  • status.allowed: boolean - True if the action is allowed
  • status.denied: boolean - True if explicitly denied by policy
  • status.reason: string - Human-readable reason for the decision
  • status.evaluationError: string - Error message if evaluation failed

Return Value

  • 200 (SelfSubjectAccessReview): OK - Request successful, permission check completed
  • 201 (SelfSubjectAccessReview): Created - Permission check successfully created
  • 202 (SelfSubjectAccessReview): Accepted - Request accepted for processing
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Check Skills Service Pod Creation Permission

This example demonstrates the Skills service checking if it can create pods in its namespace.

apiVersion: authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: SelfSubjectAccessReview
metadata:
  name: skills-pod-check
spec:
  resourceAttributes:
    namespace: skills
    verb: create
    group: ""
    version: v1
    resource: pods
# Check Skills service pod creation permission
kubectl create -f skills-pod-check.yaml
selfsubjectaccessreview.authorization.k8s.io/skills-pod-check created Status: allowed=true Reason: RBAC: allowed by RoleBinding 'skills-pod-creator'
Example 2: Check User Service Deployment Management Permission

This example shows the User service verifying deployment update permissions.

  name: user-deployment-check
spec:
  resourceAttributes:
    namespace: user
    verb: update
    group: apps
    version: v1
    resource: deployments
# Check User service deployment management permission

kubectl describe selfsubjectaccessreview user-deployment-check
selfsubjectaccessreview.authorization.k8s.io/user-deployment-check created Name: user-deployment-check API Version: authorization.k8s.io/v1 Kind: SelfSubjectAccessReview Status: Allowed: true Reason: RBAC: allowed by RoleBinding 'user-deployment-manager'
Example 3: Check Author Service Secret Read Permission

This example illustrates the Author service checking secret access permissions.

SelfSubjectAccessReviewSpec

Official Docs: SelfSubjectAccessReviewSpec v1 API | API Version: authorization.k8s.io/v1

SelfSubjectAccessReviewSpec describes the access request for the current user.

Full Description

SelfSubjectAccessReviewSpec is the specification of the permission check request for the current authenticated user. It defines what action the user wants to check permission for, using either resourceAttributes for Kubernetes resource access or nonResourceAttributes for non-resource URL paths. Exactly one of these must be set.

For your anihpj Django application services, this spec allows each service to define precisely what permission they want to verify before attempting operations, ensuring smoother operation and better error handling.

Parameters Description

  • resourceAttributes: ResourceAttributes - Describes attributes for resource-based access checks (namespace, verb, group, version, resource, subresource, name, fieldSelector, labelSelector)
  • nonResourceAttributes: NonResourceAttributes - Describes attributes for non-resource URL access checks (path, verb)

Return Value

  • SelfSubjectAccessReviewSpec: Specification object defining the permission check request

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Skills Service Resource Check Specification

This example demonstrates creating a spec for Skills service Job creation check.

spec:
  resourceAttributes:
    namespace: skills
    verb: create
    group: batch
    version: v1
    resource: jobs
# Skills service checks Job creation permission
kubectl auth can-i create jobs -n skills
yes
Example 2: User Service Specific Resource Check

This example shows a spec for checking access to a specific User deployment.

spec:
  resourceAttributes:
    namespace: user
    verb: delete
    group: apps
    version: v1
    resource: deployments
    name: anihpj-user-api
# User service checks specific deployment deletion permission
kubectl auth can-i delete deployment/anihpj-user-api -n user
no
Example 3: Author Service Non-Resource URL Check

This example illustrates a spec for checking API endpoint access.

spec:
  nonResourceAttributes:
    path: /api/v1
    verb: get
# Author service checks API endpoint access
kubectl auth can-i get /api/v1
yes
Example 4: Location Service Subresource Check

This example demonstrates checking access to a resource subresource like logs.

spec:
  resourceAttributes:
    namespace: location
    verb: get
    group: ""
    version: v1
    resource: pods
    subresource: log
# Location service checks pod log access
kubectl auth can-i get pods/log -n location
yes
Example 5: JobPost Service Cluster-Wide Check Specification

This example shows a spec for checking permissions without namespace restriction.

spec:
  resourceAttributes:
    verb: list
    group: ""
    version: v1
    resource: persistentvolumes
# JobPost service checks cluster-wide PV listing
kubectl auth can-i list persistentvolumes --all-namespaces
yes

SelfSubjectAccessReview Operations

Operations Overview

create - Create a SelfSubjectAccessReview

Operations allow you to interact with SelfSubjectAccessReview resources through the Kubernetes API. These operations enable your anihpj Django application services to validate their own permissions before performing actions, ensuring secure and error-free operations.

create - create a SelfSubjectAccessReview

Create a SelfSubjectAccessReview to check if the current user can perform an action.

HTTP Request
POST /apis/authorization.k8s.io/v1/selfsubjectaccessreviews
Parameters
  • body: SelfSubjectAccessReview, required - the permission check specification
  • dryRun (in query): string - dry run mode
  • fieldManager (in query): string - field manager name
  • fieldValidation (in query): string - field validation policy (Strict, Warn, Ignore)
  • pretty (in query): string - pretty print output
Return Value
  • 200 (SelfSubjectAccessReview): OK
  • 201 (SelfSubjectAccessReview): Created
  • 202 (SelfSubjectAccessReview): Accepted
  • 401: Unauthorized

SelfSubjectRulesReview

SelfSubjectRulesReview Overview

SelfSubjectRulesReviewSpec - Request specification
Operations - API operations for management
Official Docs: SelfSubjectRulesReview v1 API | API Version: authorization.k8s.io/v1

SelfSubjectRulesReview enumerates the set of actions the current user can perform within a namespace.

Full Description

SelfSubjectRulesReview provides a comprehensive list of all actions (rules) that the current authenticated user can perform within a specific namespace. This is particularly useful for UIs to show or hide actions based on user permissions, and for users to quickly understand what they're allowed to do.

For your anihpj Django application, this resource helps services discover their complete permission sets within namespaces. For example, the Skills, User, Author, Location, and JobPost services can query their full list of allowed actions, making it easier to implement dynamic UI behaviors and permission-aware features. The returned list may be incomplete depending on the server's authorization mode.

Important Note: SelfSubjectRulesReview is designed for UI display and user reasoning, NOT for driving authorization decisions by external systems. For authorization decisions, use SubjectAccessReview or LocalSubjectAccessReview instead.

Key Features:

  • Complete Rule Enumeration: Lists all allowed actions for the current user in a namespace
  • Resource and Non-Resource Rules: Covers both Kubernetes resource actions and API endpoint access
  • UI-Friendly: Perfect for showing/hiding UI elements based on permissions
  • Self-Discovery: Users can discover their own permissions without admin help
  • Incomplete Indication: Flags when the rule list may not be complete

Syntax

# Create SelfSubjectRulesReview from YAML file
kubectl create -f selfsubjectrulesreview.yaml
# View the returned rules
kubectl describe selfsubjectrulesreview [name]
# Check rules in JSON format
kubectl create -f selfsubjectrulesreview.yaml -o json

YAML Structure

apiVersion: authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: SelfSubjectRulesReview

metadata:
  name: string

spec:
  namespace: string

status:
  incomplete: boolean
  resourceRules:
  - verbs: []string
    apiGroups: []string
    resources: []string
    resourceNames: []string
  nonResourceRules:
  - verbs: []string
    nonResourceURLs: []string
  evaluationError: string

Parameters Description

  • apiVersion: string - API version, always "authorization.k8s.io/v1" for SelfSubjectRulesReview
  • kind: string - Resource type, always "SelfSubjectRulesReview"
  • metadata: ObjectMeta - Standard object metadata
  • spec: SelfSubjectRulesReviewSpec (required) - Specification of the rules review request
  • spec.namespace: string (required) - Namespace to evaluate rules for
  • status: SubjectRulesReviewStatus - Result of the rules check (populated by API server)
  • status.incomplete: boolean (required) - True when returned rules are incomplete
  • status.resourceRules: []ResourceRule (required) - List of allowed actions on resources
  • status.nonResourceRules: []NonResourceRule (required) - List of allowed actions on non-resources
  • status.evaluationError: string - Error message if rule evaluation failed

Return Value

  • 200 (SelfSubjectRulesReview): OK - Request successful, rules enumerated
  • 201 (SelfSubjectRulesReview): Created - Rules review successfully created
  • 202 (SelfSubjectRulesReview): Accepted - Request accepted for processing
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Skills Service Discovers All Permissions

This example demonstrates the Skills service enumerating all its permissions in the skills namespace.

apiVersion: authorization.k8s.io/v1

metadata:
  name: skills-rules-check
spec:
  namespace: skills
# Skills service discovers all permissions
kubectl create -f skills-rules-check.yaml -o yaml

  namespace: user

SelfSubjectRulesReviewSpec

Official Docs: SelfSubjectRulesReviewSpec v1 API | API Version: authorization.k8s.io/v1

SelfSubjectRulesReviewSpec defines the specification for SelfSubjectRulesReview.

Full Description

SelfSubjectRulesReviewSpec is the specification for a rules review request. It contains only one field: the namespace in which to evaluate the current user's permissions. This simple spec makes it easy to discover all allowed actions within a specific namespace scope.

For your anihpj Django application services, this spec allows each service to specify which namespace they want to check permissions for, enabling namespace-scoped permission discovery for better access control management.

Parameters Description

  • namespace: string (required) - The namespace to evaluate rules for

Return Value

  • SelfSubjectRulesReviewSpec: Specification object defining the namespace for rules evaluation

apiVersion: authorization.k8s.io/v1 kind: SelfSubjectRulesReview metadata: name: author-secret-rules status: incomplete: false resourceRules: - verbs: ["get", "list"] apiGroups: [""] resources: ["secrets"] - verbs: ["get", "list", "watch"] apiGroups: [""] resources: ["configmaps"]

apiVersion: authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: SelfSubjectRulesReview
metadata:
  name: location-storage-rules
spec:
  namespace: location
# Location service checks storage rules
