SubjectAccessReview

SubjectAccessReview Overview

SubjectAccessReviewSpec - Access request parameters
SubjectAccessReviewStatus - Authorization decision
Operations - API operations for management
Official Docs: SubjectAccessReview v1 API | API Version: authorization.k8s.io/v1

SubjectAccessReview checks whether a specified user, group, or service account can perform an action - privileged operation for administrators.

Full Description

SubjectAccessReview checks whether or not a specified user, group, or service account can perform an action. Unlike SelfSubjectAccessReview which only checks the current user's permissions, SubjectAccessReview is a privileged operation that allows administrators to verify what actions other subjects can perform. This is commonly used by administrators to validate RBAC configurations, troubleshoot permission issues, and verify that security policies are correctly enforced before granting access to resources.

In your anihpj Django application, cluster administrators can use SubjectAccessReview to verify permissions for Skills, User, Author, Location, and JobPost service accounts before deploying critical workloads. This ensures that RBAC policies are correctly configured and that services have exactly the permissions they need—no more, no less—following the principle of least privilege for enhanced security.

Syntax

# Create a SubjectAccessReview from YAML file
kubectl create -f subjectaccessreview.yaml
# Check if a user can perform an action
kubectl auth can-i --list --as={user}
# Check specific permission for a user
kubectl auth can-i {verb} {resource} --as={user}
# Check permission in specific namespace
kubectl auth can-i {verb} {resource} --as={user} -n {namespace}

YAML Structure

apiVersion: authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: SubjectAccessReview
metadata:
  name: check-user-permissions
spec:
  user: system:serviceaccount:default:anihpj-skills-sa
  groups:
  - system:serviceaccounts
  - system:authenticated
  resourceAttributes:
    namespace: default
    verb: create
    group: apps
    version: v1
    resource: deployments
status:
  allowed: true
  reason: "RBAC: allowed by RoleBinding"

Parameters Description

  • spec.user: User identity to check permissions for. If specified without groups, checks permissions as if user has no group memberships.
  • spec.groups: Groups the user belongs to for authorization check. Corresponds to user.Info.GetGroups().
  • spec.extra: Additional information about the user. Corresponds to user.Info.GetExtra() from the authenticator.
  • spec.uid: UID information about the requesting user.
  • spec.resourceAttributes: Describes resource access request (mutually exclusive with nonResourceAttributes).
  • spec.nonResourceAttributes: Describes non-resource access request like /api or /healthz (mutually exclusive with resourceAttributes).
  • status.allowed: True if the action would be allowed, false otherwise (required).
  • status.denied: True if action explicitly denied. Can be false while allowed is also false if authorizer has no opinion.
  • status.reason: Human-readable explanation for authorization decision.
  • status.evaluationError: Indicates errors during authorization check. Authorization may still be determined despite errors.

Return Value

  • 200 (SubjectAccessReview): OK - Request successful, SubjectAccessReview returned
  • 201 (SubjectAccessReview): Created - SubjectAccessReview successfully created
  • 202 (SubjectAccessReview): Accepted - Request accepted for processing
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required

SubjectAccessReviewSpec

Official Docs: SubjectAccessReviewSpec v1 API | API Version: authorization.k8s.io/v1

SubjectAccessReviewSpec describes the access request being evaluated for authorization.

Full Description

SubjectAccessReviewSpec is a description of the access request being evaluated. It specifies the subject (user, groups, service account) and the action they want to perform. Exactly one of resourceAttributes or nonResourceAttributes must be set - resourceAttributes for checking access to Kubernetes resources (like pods, deployments) and nonResourceAttributes for checking access to non-resource URLs (like /api, /healthz, /metrics). The spec includes user identity information, group memberships, and optional extra attributes that may be used by custom authorizers.

Parameters Description

  • user: string - User identity to check permissions for. If specified without groups, checks as if user has no groups
  • groups: []string - Groups the user belongs to. Corresponds to user.Info.GetGroups() from authenticator
  • extra: map[string][]string - Extra information about the user. Corresponds to user.Info.GetExtra() method
  • uid: string - UID information about the requesting user
  • resourceAttributes: ResourceAttributes - Information for resource access request (mutually exclusive with nonResourceAttributes)
  • resourceAttributes.namespace: string - Namespace of the resource. Empty means "all" for cluster-scoped or all namespaces
  • resourceAttributes.verb: string - Kubernetes API verb: get, list, watch, create, update, delete, patch, proxy. "*" means all
  • resourceAttributes.group: string - API Group of the resource. "*" means all. Empty for core API
  • resourceAttributes.version: string - API Version of the resource. "*" means all
  • resourceAttributes.resource: string - Resource type (pods, deployments, etc). "*" means all
  • resourceAttributes.subresource: string - Subresource (status, scale, etc). Empty means none
  • resourceAttributes.name: string - Name of specific resource instance. Empty means all
  • nonResourceAttributes: NonResourceAttributes - Information for non-resource URL access (mutually exclusive with resourceAttributes)
  • nonResourceAttributes.path: string - URL path of request (/api, /healthz, /metrics)
  • nonResourceAttributes.verb: string - Standard HTTP verb (get, post, put, delete, patch)

Return Value

  • Part of SubjectAccessReview - SubjectAccessReviewSpec is processed by the server which populates the status field

SubjectAccessReviewStatus

Official Docs: SubjectAccessReviewStatus v1 API | API Version: authorization.k8s.io/v1

SubjectAccessReviewStatus contains the server's authorization decision with allowed/denied status.

Full Description

SubjectAccessReviewStatus is filled in by the server and indicates whether the requested action is allowed or not. The status includes the authorization decision (allowed or denied), an optional human-readable reason explaining the decision, and an optional evaluation error field for cases where errors occurred during authorization processing. Note that both allowed and denied can be false simultaneously, indicating that the authorizer has no opinion on the request. An action may still be determined despite evaluation errors, as authorization systems like RBAC can make decisions even when some roles are missing.

Parameters Description

  • allowed: boolean (required) - True if the action would be allowed, false otherwise
  • denied: boolean - True if action explicitly denied. Can be false while allowed is also false if authorizer has no opinion
  • reason: string - Human-readable explanation for the authorization decision. Typically contains RBAC rule information
  • evaluationError: string - Indicates errors during authorization check. Authorization may still be determined despite errors (e.g., RBAC missing a role but enough roles present to decide)

Return Value

  • Part of SubjectAccessReview - SubjectAccessReviewStatus is populated by the server in the returned SubjectAccessReview object

SubjectAccessReview Operations

Operations Overview

create - Create a SubjectAccessReview

SubjectAccessReview operations allow cluster administrators to check whether other users, groups, or service accounts can perform specific actions. This privileged operation is essential for validating RBAC configurations in your anihpj Django application.

create - create a SubjectAccessReview

Create a SubjectAccessReview to check if a specified subject can perform an action.

HTTP Request
POST /apis/authorization.k8s.io/v1/subjectaccessreviews
Parameters
  • body: SubjectAccessReview, required - SubjectAccessReview object to create
  • dryRun (in query): string - When present, indicates request should not be persisted
  • fieldManager (in query): string - Name of the manager associated with this operation
  • fieldValidation (in query): string - Field validation level (Ignore, Warn, Strict)
  • pretty (in query): string - If true, return pretty-printed output
Return Value
  • 200 (SubjectAccessReview): OK
  • 201 (SubjectAccessReview): Created
  • 202 (SubjectAccessReview): Accepted
  • 401: Unauthorized

ClusterRole

ClusterRole Overview

ClusterRoleList - Collection of ClusterRoles
Operations - API operations for management
Official Docs: ClusterRole v1 API | API Version: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1

ClusterRole is a cluster level, logical grouping of PolicyRules that can be referenced as a unit by a RoleBinding or ClusterRoleBinding.

Full Description

ClusterRole is a cluster-scoped resource that defines a set of permissions (PolicyRules) for accessing Kubernetes resources across all namespaces. Unlike Roles which are namespace-scoped, ClusterRoles can grant access to cluster-scoped resources (like nodes, persistent volumes) or be used across all namespaces. ClusterRoles support aggregation through AggregationRule, allowing you to compose permissions from multiple ClusterRoles dynamically. This is commonly used by cluster administrators to define reusable permission sets for RBAC (Role-Based Access Control) configurations.

In your anihpj Django application, ClusterRoles define permissions for Skills, User, Author, Location, and JobPost service accounts to access cluster-wide resources. For example, you might create a ClusterRole that allows reading all ConfigMaps across namespaces, or managing persistent volumes for database storage. ClusterRoles are bound to subjects (users, groups, or service accounts) using ClusterRoleBindings for cluster-wide access, or RoleBindings for namespace-specific access.

Syntax

# Create a ClusterRole from YAML file
kubectl create -f clusterrole.yaml
# Get a specific ClusterRole
kubectl get clusterrole {name}
# List all ClusterRoles
kubectl get clusterroles
# Delete a ClusterRole
kubectl delete clusterrole {name}

YAML Structure

apiVersion: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: ClusterRole
metadata:
  name: anihpj-cluster-reader
  labels:
    app: anihpj
rules:
- apiGroups: [""]
  resources: ["pods", "services", "configmaps"]
  verbs: ["get", "list", "watch"]
- apiGroups: ["apps"]
  resources: ["deployments", "statefulsets"]
  verbs: ["get", "list"]

Parameters Description

  • apiVersion: string - API version (rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1)
  • kind: string - Resource type (ClusterRole)
  • metadata: ObjectMeta - Standard object's metadata including name, labels, annotations
  • aggregationRule: AggregationRule - Optional field that describes how to build Rules from other ClusterRoles
  • aggregationRule.clusterRoleSelectors: []LabelSelector - Selectors to find ClusterRoles and aggregate their rules
  • rules: []PolicyRule - List of PolicyRules for this ClusterRole (controller managed if aggregationRule is set)
  • rules.apiGroups: []string - API groups that contain the resources ("" for core, "*" for all)
  • rules.resources: []string - List of resources this rule applies to ("*" for all resources)
  • rules.verbs: []string, required - List of verbs (get, list, create, update, delete, "*" for all)
  • rules.resourceNames: []string - Optional whitelist of specific resource names
  • rules.nonResourceURLs: []string - Partial URLs for non-resource access (only for ClusterRoleBindings)

Return Value

  • ClusterRole: Returns ClusterRole object with metadata, rules, and aggregation configuration
  • Status: HTTP status codes (200 OK, 201 Created, 401 Unauthorized, 404 Not Found)

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Create ClusterRole for Skills Service Read Access

This example creates a ClusterRole allowing Skills service to read ConfigMaps and Secrets across all namespaces.

# skills-reader-clusterrole.yaml

  labels:
    app: anihpj
    model: skills
    component: rbac
rules:
- apiGroups: [""]
  resources: ["configmaps", "secrets"]
  verbs: ["get", "list", "watch"]

Example 3: Create Aggregated ClusterRole for Author Service

This example demonstrates creating a ClusterRole that aggregates permissions from other ClusterRoles.

# author-aggregated-clusterrole.yaml
apiVersion: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: ClusterRole
metadata:
  name: anihpj-author-aggregated
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    model: author
    rbac.anihpj.io/aggregate-to-author: "true"
aggregationRule:
  clusterRoleSelectors:
  - matchLabels:
      rbac.anihpj.io/aggregate-to-author: "true"
rules: []
# Create the aggregated ClusterRole
kubectl create -f author-aggregated-clusterrole.yaml
kubectl get clusterrole anihpj-author-aggregated -o yaml
clusterrole.rbac.authorization.k8s.io/anihpj-author-aggregated created apiVersion: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1 kind: ClusterRole metadata: name: anihpj-author-aggregated labels: app: anihpj model: author rbac.anihpj.io/aggregate-to-author: "true" aggregationRule: clusterRoleSelectors: - matchLabels: rbac.anihpj.io/aggregate-to-author: "true" rules: - apiGroups: [""] resources: ["pods", "configmaps"] verbs: ["get", "list"]

Example 5: Create ClusterRole for JobPost Service with Non-Resource URLs

This example shows creating a ClusterRole for JobPost service to access API discovery endpoints.

# jobpost-api-discovery-clusterrole.yaml

ClusterRoleList

Official Docs: ClusterRoleList v1 API | API Version: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1

ClusterRoleList is a collection of ClusterRoles returned by list operations.

Full Description

ClusterRoleList is a collection object that contains an array of ClusterRole resources. It is returned when you list all ClusterRoles in the cluster using kubectl or the Kubernetes API. The list includes standard metadata and an items array containing all ClusterRole objects that match the query parameters. This is useful for discovering available cluster-wide permissions, auditing RBAC configurations, and managing authorization policies across your Kubernetes cluster.

Parameters Description

  • apiVersion: string - API version (rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1)
  • kind: string - Resource type (ClusterRoleList)
  • metadata: ListMeta - Standard list metadata including resource version and continue token
  • items: []ClusterRole, required - Array of ClusterRole objects

Return Value

  • ClusterRoleList: Returns collection with metadata and items array of ClusterRoles
  • Status: HTTP status codes (200 OK, 401 Unauthorized)

ClusterRole Operations

Operations Overview

get - Read the specified ClusterRole
list - List or watch objects of kind ClusterRole
create - Create a ClusterRole
update - Replace the specified ClusterRole
patch - Partially update the specified ClusterRole
delete - Delete a ClusterRole
deletecollection - Delete collection of ClusterRole

ClusterRole operations allow cluster administrators to manage cluster-wide RBAC permissions for your anihpj Django application. These operations enable you to define, update, and delete permission sets that can be assigned to service accounts across all namespaces.

get - read the specified ClusterRole

Read the specified ClusterRole by name.

HTTP Request
GET /apis/rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1/clusterroles/{name}
Parameters
  • name (in path): string, required - Name of the ClusterRole
  • pretty (in query): string - Pretty print output
Return Value
  • 200 (ClusterRole): OK
  • 401: Unauthorized

HTTP Request

  • allowWatchBookmarks (in query): boolean - Enable watch bookmarks
  • continue (in query): string - Continue token for pagination
  • fieldSelector (in query): string - Field selector for filtering
  • labelSelector (in query): string - Label selector for filtering
  • limit (in query): integer - Maximum number of results to return
  • pretty (in query): string - Pretty print output
  • resourceVersion (in query): string - Resource version for list
  • timeoutSeconds (in query): integer - Timeout for the list/watch call
  • watch (in query): boolean - Watch for changes

  • 200 (ClusterRoleList): OK
  • 401: Unauthorized

RoleBinding

RoleBinding Overview

RoleBindingList - Collection of RoleBindings
Operations - API operations for management
Official Docs: RoleBinding v1 API | API Version: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1

RoleBinding references a role, but does not contain it.

Full Description

RoleBinding references a role, but does not contain it. It can reference a Role in the same namespace or a ClusterRole in the global namespace. It adds who information via Subjects and namespace information by which namespace it exists in. RoleBindings in a given namespace only have effect in that namespace.

Syntax

apiVersion: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: RoleBinding
metadata:
  name: rolebinding-name
  namespace: namespace-name
roleRef:
  apiGroup: rbac.authorization.k8s.io
  kind: Role
  name: role-name
subjects:
- kind: ServiceAccount
  name: serviceaccount-name
  namespace: namespace-name

YAML Structure

apiVersion: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: RoleBinding
metadata: ObjectMeta
roleRef: RoleRef
subjects: []Subject

Parameters Description

metadata (ObjectMeta): Standard object's metadata.

roleRef (RoleRef), required: RoleRef can reference a Role in the current namespace or a ClusterRole in the global namespace. If the RoleRef cannot be resolved, the Authorizer must return an error. This field is immutable.

  • roleRef.apiGroup (string), required: APIGroup is the group for the resource being referenced
  • roleRef.kind (string), required: Kind is the type of resource being referenced
  • roleRef.name (string), required: Name is the name of resource being referenced

subjects ([]Subject): Atomic: will be replaced during a merge. Subjects holds references to the objects the role applies to.

  • subjects.kind (string), required: Kind of object being referenced. Values defined by this API group are "User", "Group", and "ServiceAccount". If the Authorizer does not recognized the kind value, the Authorizer should report an error.
  • subjects.name (string), required: Name of the object being referenced.
  • subjects.apiGroup (string): APIGroup holds the API group of the referenced subject. Defaults to "" for ServiceAccount subjects. Defaults to "rbac.authorization.k8s.io" for User and Group subjects.
  • subjects.namespace (string): Namespace of the referenced object. If the object kind is non-namespace, such as "User" or "Group", and this value is not empty the Authorizer should report an error.

Return Value

  • RoleBinding: Returns RoleBinding object with metadata, roleRef, and subjects configuration
  • 200: OK
  • 201: Created
  • 401: Unauthorized

Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Bind Skills Manager Role to Service Account

This example creates a RoleBinding that grants Skills model management permissions to a service account.

# Create RoleBinding for Skills manager
kubectl create rolebinding skills-manager-binding \
  --role=skills-admin \
  --serviceaccount=anihpj:skills-service-account \
  --namespace=anihpj
rolebinding.rbac.authorization.k8s.io/skills-manager-binding created
Example 2: Bind User Read Role to Group

This example creates a RoleBinding that grants User model read permissions to a user group.

# Create RoleBinding for User readers
kubectl create rolebinding user-reader-binding \
  --role=user-reader \
  --group=user-viewers \
  --namespace=anihpj
rolebinding.rbac.authorization.k8s.io/user-reader-binding created
Example 3: Bind Author Editor Role to User

This example creates a RoleBinding that grants Author model edit permissions to a specific user.

# Create RoleBinding for Author editor
kubectl create rolebinding author-editor-binding \
  --role=author-editor \
  --user=john@anihpj.com \
  --namespace=anihpj
rolebinding.rbac.authorization.k8s.io/author-editor-binding created
Example 4: Bind Location Admin Role with YAML

This example creates a RoleBinding using YAML manifest for Location model admin permissions.

# Create RoleBinding from YAML
cat <<EOF | kubectl apply -f -
apiVersion: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: RoleBinding
metadata:
  name: location-admin-binding
  namespace: anihpj
roleRef:
  apiGroup: rbac.authorization.k8s.io
  kind: Role
  name: location-admin
subjects:
- kind: ServiceAccount
  name: location-service-account
  namespace: anihpj
EOF
rolebinding.rbac.authorization.k8s.io/location-admin-binding created
Example 5: Bind JobPost Publisher Role to Multiple Subjects

This example creates a RoleBinding that grants JobPost publishing permissions to multiple subjects.

# Create RoleBinding with multiple subjects
cat <<EOF | kubectl apply -f -
apiVersion: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: RoleBinding
metadata:
  name: jobpost-publisher-binding
  namespace: anihpj
roleRef:
  apiGroup: rbac.authorization.k8s.io
  kind: Role
  name: jobpost-publisher
subjects:
- kind: ServiceAccount
  name: jobpost-service-account
  namespace: anihpj
- kind: User
  name: admin@anihpj.com
  apiGroup: rbac.authorization.k8s.io
- kind: Group
  name: publishers
  apiGroup: rbac.authorization.k8s.io
EOF
rolebinding.rbac.authorization.k8s.io/jobpost-publisher-binding created

RoleBindingList

RoleBindingList is a collection of RoleBindings

YAML Structure

apiVersion: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: RoleBindingList
metadata: ListMeta
items: []RoleBinding

Parameters Description

metadata (ListMeta): Standard object's metadata.

items ([]RoleBinding), required: Items is a list of RoleBindings

Return Value

  • RoleBindingList: Returns a list of RoleBinding objects
  • 200: OK
  • 401: Unauthorized

Practical Django Examples

Example 1: List All RoleBindings in Namespace

This example lists all RoleBindings in the anihpj namespace.

# List all RoleBindings
kubectl get rolebindings -n anihpj
NAME ROLE AGE skills-manager-binding Role/skills-admin 5d user-reader-binding Role/user-reader 3d author-editor-binding Role/author-editor 2d location-admin-binding Role/location-admin 1d jobpost-publisher-binding Role/jobpost-publisher 12h
Example 2: List RoleBindings with Custom Columns

This example lists RoleBindings showing specific columns.

# List RoleBindings with custom output
kubectl get rolebindings -n anihpj -o custom-columns=NAME:.metadata.name,ROLE:.roleRef.name,KIND:.roleRef.kind
NAME ROLE KIND skills-manager-binding skills-admin Role user-reader-binding user-reader Role author-editor-binding author-editor Role location-admin-binding location-admin Role jobpost-publisher-binding jobpost-publisher Role
Example 3: List RoleBindings in YAML Format

This example retrieves the complete RoleBindingList in YAML format.

# Get RoleBindingList in YAML
kubectl get rolebindings -n anihpj -o yaml
apiVersion: v1 items: - apiVersion: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1 kind: RoleBinding metadata: name: skills-manager-binding namespace: anihpj roleRef: apiGroup: rbac.authorization.k8s.io kind: Role name: skills-admin subjects: - kind: ServiceAccount name: skills-service-account namespace: anihpj kind: List metadata: resourceVersion: ""
Example 4: Filter RoleBindings by Label

This example lists RoleBindings filtered by model label.

# List RoleBindings with label filter
kubectl get rolebindings -n anihpj -l app=jobpost
NAME ROLE AGE jobpost-publisher-binding Role/jobpost-publisher 12h
Example 5: Watch RoleBindings for Changes

This example watches for changes to RoleBindings in real-time.

# Watch RoleBindings
kubectl get rolebindings -n anihpj --watch
NAME ROLE AGE skills-manager-binding Role/skills-admin 5d user-reader-binding Role/user-reader 3d ADDED author-editor-binding Role/author-editor 0s MODIFIED skills-manager-binding Role/skills-admin 5d

RoleBinding Operations

Operations Overview
get - Read the specified RoleBinding
list - List RoleBindings (namespace)
list - List RoleBindings (all namespaces)
create - Create a RoleBinding
update - Replace the specified RoleBinding
patch - Partially update the specified RoleBinding
delete - Delete a RoleBinding
deletecollection - Delete collection of RoleBinding
get - read the specified RoleBinding
HTTP Request
GET /apis/rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/rolebindings/{name}
Parameters
  • name (in path): string, required - name of the RoleBinding
  • namespace (in path): string, required - namespace
  • pretty (in query): string - pretty
Return Value
  • 200 (RoleBinding): OK
  • 401: Unauthorized

This example completely replaces the User RoleBinding configuration.

# Replace RoleBinding

apiVersion: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: RoleBinding
metadata:
  name: user-reader-binding
  namespace: anihpj
  labels:
    app: user
    updated: "true"
roleRef:
  apiGroup: rbac.authorization.k8s.io
  kind: Role
  name: user-reader-v2
subjects:
- kind: Group
  name: user-viewers-updated
  apiGroup: rbac.authorization.k8s.io
EOF
rolebinding.rbac.authorization.k8s.io/user-reader-binding replaced

This example adds annotations to the Author RoleBinding.

# Patch annotations
kubectl patch rolebinding author-editor-binding -n anihpj --type='merge' -p='
{
  "metadata": {
    "annotations": {
      "description": "Author model editor permissions",
      "managed-by": "anihpj-controller"
    }
  }
}'
rolebinding.rbac.authorization.k8s.io/author-editor-binding patched
Example 4: Update Location RoleBinding Subject

This example replaces the subject in Location RoleBinding using JSON patch.

# Replace subject with JSON patch
kubectl patch rolebinding location-admin-binding -n anihpj --type='json' -p='[
  {"op": "replace", "path": "/subjects/0/name", "value": "location-service-account-v2"}
]'
rolebinding.rbac.authorization.k8s.io/location-admin-binding patched
Example 5: Patch JobPost RoleBinding with Multiple Operations

This example applies multiple patch operations to JobPost RoleBinding.

# Multiple patch operations
kubectl patch rolebinding jobpost-publisher-binding -n anihpj --type='json' -p='[
  {"op": "add", "path": "/metadata/labels/tier", "value": "backend"},
  {"op": "add", "path": "/metadata/annotations/updated", "value": "2025-01-10"}
]'
rolebinding.rbac.authorization.k8s.io/jobpost-publisher-binding patched

ClusterRoleBinding

ClusterRoleBinding Overview

ClusterRoleBindingList - Collection of ClusterRoleBindings
Operations - API operations for management
Official Docs: ClusterRoleBinding v1 API | API Version: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1

ClusterRoleBinding references a ClusterRole and grants cluster-wide permissions to subjects (users, groups, or service accounts).

Full Description

ClusterRoleBinding is a cluster-scoped resource that binds a ClusterRole to subjects (users, groups, or service accounts), granting them the permissions defined in the ClusterRole across the entire cluster. Unlike RoleBinding which is namespace-scoped, ClusterRoleBinding applies permissions cluster-wide, making it suitable for admin users, system components, or services that need to access resources across all namespaces. The ClusterRoleBinding references a ClusterRole by name and lists the subjects that should receive those permissions.

In your anihpj Django application, ClusterRoleBindings are essential for granting cluster-wide permissions to your Skills, User, Author, Location, and JobPost service accounts. For example, you might create a ClusterRoleBinding that grants the Skills service account permission to read ConfigMaps across all namespaces, or allows the JobPost service to manage persistent volumes cluster-wide. This enables your Django services to operate seamlessly across namespace boundaries when needed.

Syntax

# Create a ClusterRoleBinding from YAML file
kubectl create -f clusterrolebinding.yaml
# Create a ClusterRoleBinding imperatively
kubectl create clusterrolebinding {name} --clusterrole={role} --serviceaccount={namespace}:{sa-name}
# List all ClusterRoleBindings
kubectl get clusterrolebindings
# List all ClusterRoleBindings (short form)
kubectl get crb
# Get detailed information about a specific ClusterRoleBinding
kubectl describe clusterrolebinding {name}
# Get detailed information about a specific ClusterRoleBinding (short form)
kubectl describe crb {name}
# Get ClusterRoleBinding in YAML format
kubectl get clusterrolebinding {name} -o yaml
# Delete a specific ClusterRoleBinding
kubectl delete clusterrolebinding {name}
# Delete a specific ClusterRoleBinding (short form)
kubectl delete crb {name}

YAML Structure

apiVersion: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: ClusterRoleBinding
metadata:
  name: anihpj-skills-cluster-admin
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    model: skills
subjects:
- kind: ServiceAccount
  name: anihpj-skills-sa
  namespace: default
roleRef:
  kind: ClusterRole
  name: cluster-admin
  apiGroup: rbac.authorization.k8s.io

Parameters Description

  • apiVersion: string - API version (rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1)
  • kind: string - Resource type (ClusterRoleBinding)
  • metadata: ObjectMeta - Standard object's metadata including name, labels, annotations
  • subjects: []Subject - List of subjects (users, groups, service accounts) to bind the ClusterRole to
  • subjects.kind: string, required - Kind of subject (User, Group, ServiceAccount)
  • subjects.name: string, required - Name of the subject
  • subjects.namespace: string - Namespace of the subject (required for ServiceAccount)
  • subjects.apiGroup: string - API group of the subject (defaults to "" for ServiceAccount)
  • roleRef: RoleRef, required - Reference to the ClusterRole to bind
  • roleRef.kind: string, required - Must be "ClusterRole"
  • roleRef.name: string, required - Name of the ClusterRole
  • roleRef.apiGroup: string, required - Must be "rbac.authorization.k8s.io"

Return Value

  • 200 (ClusterRoleBinding): OK - Request successful, ClusterRoleBinding returned
  • 201 (ClusterRoleBinding): Created - ClusterRoleBinding successfully created
  • 202 (ClusterRoleBinding): Accepted - Request accepted for processing
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Bind Skills Service Account to ConfigMap Reader ClusterRole

This example creates a ClusterRoleBinding granting Skills service cluster-wide ConfigMap read access.

# skills-configmap-binding.yaml
apiVersion: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: ClusterRoleBinding
metadata:
  name: anihpj-skills-configmap-reader
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    model: skills
    component: rbac
subjects:
- kind: ServiceAccount
  name: anihpj-skills-sa
  namespace: default
roleRef:
  kind: ClusterRole
  name: anihpj-skills-reader
  apiGroup: rbac.authorization.k8s.io
# Create ClusterRoleBinding for Skills service
kubectl create -f skills-configmap-binding.yaml
# Verify the ClusterRoleBinding was created
kubectl get clusterrolebinding anihpj-skills-configmap-reader
clusterrolebinding.rbac.authorization.k8s.io/anihpj-skills-configmap-reader created NAME ROLE AGE anihpj-skills-configmap-reader ClusterRole/anihpj-skills-reader 5s
Example 2: Bind User Service Account to Deployment Manager ClusterRole

This example shows binding User service account to manage deployments cluster-wide.

metadata:
  name: anihpj-user-deployment-manager
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    model: user
    environment: production
subjects:
- kind: ServiceAccount
  name: anihpj-user-sa
  namespace: default
roleRef:
  kind: ClusterRole
  name: anihpj-user-manager
  apiGroup: rbac.authorization.k8s.io
# Create ClusterRoleBinding for User service

Example 5: Bind JobPost Service to API Discovery ClusterRole

This example shows binding JobPost service account to API discovery ClusterRole with User and Group subjects.

# jobpost-api-discovery-binding.yaml
apiVersion: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: ClusterRoleBinding
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-api-discovery
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    model: jobpost
    security: api-access
subjects:
- kind: ServiceAccount
  name: anihpj-jobpost-sa
  namespace: default
- kind: User
  name: jobpost-admin
  apiGroup: rbac.authorization.k8s.io
- kind: Group
  name: anihpj-developers
  apiGroup: rbac.authorization.k8s.io
roleRef:
  kind: ClusterRole
  name: anihpj-jobpost-api-discovery
  apiGroup: rbac.authorization.k8s.io
# Create ClusterRoleBinding with multiple subject types for JobPost service
kubectl create -f jobpost-api-discovery-binding.yaml
# Get detailed information about the ClusterRoleBinding
kubectl describe clusterrolebinding anihpj-jobpost-api-discovery
clusterrolebinding.rbac.authorization.k8s.io/anihpj-jobpost-api-discovery created Name: anihpj-jobpost-api-discovery Labels: app=anihpj model=jobpost security=api-access Role: Kind: ClusterRole Name: anihpj-jobpost-api-discovery Subjects: Kind Name Namespace ---- ---- --------- ServiceAccount anihpj-jobpost-sa default User jobpost-admin Group anihpj-developers

ClusterRoleBindingList

Official Docs: ClusterRoleBindingList v1 API | API Version: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1

ClusterRoleBindingList is a collection of ClusterRoleBinding objects returned by list operations.

Full Description

ClusterRoleBindingList represents a collection of ClusterRoleBindings in your Kubernetes cluster. When you query for multiple ClusterRoleBindings using kubectl or the Kubernetes API, the response is returned as a ClusterRoleBindingList object. This is particularly useful for auditing cluster-wide permissions across all services in your anihpj Django application, allowing you to view and manage ClusterRoleBindings for Skills, User, Author, Location, and JobPost service accounts simultaneously.

Parameters Description

  • apiVersion: string - API version (rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1)
  • kind: string - Resource type (ClusterRoleBindingList)
  • metadata: ListMeta - Standard list metadata including resourceVersion and continue token
  • items: []ClusterRoleBinding, required - Array of ClusterRoleBinding objects

Return Value

  • 200 (ClusterRoleBindingList): OK - Request successful, list of ClusterRoleBindings returned
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required

ClusterRoleBinding Operations

Operations Overview

get - Read the specified ClusterRoleBinding
list - List or watch objects of kind ClusterRoleBinding
create - Create a ClusterRoleBinding
update - Replace the specified ClusterRoleBinding
patch - Partially update the specified ClusterRoleBinding
delete - Delete a ClusterRoleBinding
deletecollection - Delete collection of ClusterRoleBinding

These operations allow you to manage ClusterRoleBinding resources in your Kubernetes cluster through the Kubernetes API.

get - Read the specified ClusterRoleBinding

HTTP Request: GET /apis/rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1/clusterrolebindings/{name} | kubectl: kubectl get clusterrolebinding {name}
Full Description

The get operation retrieves a specific ClusterRoleBinding resource by name from your Kubernetes cluster. This operation is essential for inspecting cluster-wide role binding configurations and understanding which subjects have been granted which permissions. When you need to verify or troubleshoot cluster access permissions for your anihpj Django services, this operation provides detailed information about the binding relationship between ClusterRoles and subjects.

Syntax
# Get specific ClusterRoleBinding
kubectl get clusterrolebinding {name}
# Get with output format
kubectl get clusterrolebinding {name} -o yaml
Parameters Description
  • name: string, required - Name of the ClusterRoleBinding to retrieve
  • pretty: string - Pretty-print the output
  • exact: boolean - Exact resource version match
  • export: boolean - Export the object stripped of cluster-specific information
Return Value
  • 200 (ClusterRoleBinding): OK - ClusterRoleBinding object retrieved successfully
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required
  • 404: Not Found - ClusterRoleBinding with specified name does not exist

list - List or watch objects of kind ClusterRoleBinding

HTTP Request: GET /apis/rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1/clusterrolebindings | kubectl: kubectl get clusterrolebindings
Full Description

The list operation retrieves all ClusterRoleBinding resources in your Kubernetes cluster or watches for changes to ClusterRoleBindings. This is crucial for cluster-wide permission audits and monitoring role binding changes across your entire anihpj Django application infrastructure. You can filter results using label selectors to focus on specific service accounts or models in your application.

Syntax
# List all ClusterRoleBindings
kubectl get clusterrolebindings
# List with label selector
kubectl get clusterrolebindings -l app=anihpj
# Watch for changes
kubectl get clusterrolebindings -w
Parameters Description
  • labelSelector: string - Selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their labels
  • fieldSelector: string - Selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their fields
  • watch: boolean - Watch for changes to the described resources
  • limit: integer - Maximum number of responses to return for a list call
  • continue: string - Token for retrieving the next chunk of results
Return Value
  • 200 (ClusterRoleBindingList): OK - List of ClusterRoleBindings returned successfully
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required

create - Create a ClusterRoleBinding

HTTP Request: POST /apis/rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1/clusterrolebindings | kubectl: kubectl create -f clusterrolebinding.yaml
Full Description

The create operation creates a new ClusterRoleBinding resource in your Kubernetes cluster, establishing cluster-wide permissions for subjects by binding them to a ClusterRole. This is essential when deploying new services in your anihpj Django application that need cluster-wide access permissions. Each ClusterRoleBinding must have a unique name and properly reference existing ClusterRoles and valid subjects.

Syntax
# Create from YAML file
kubectl create -f clusterrolebinding.yaml
# Create using kubectl create clusterrolebinding command
kubectl create clusterrolebinding {name} --clusterrole={role} --serviceaccount={namespace}:{sa-name}
Parameters Description
  • body: ClusterRoleBinding, required - ClusterRoleBinding object to create
  • dryRun: string - Dry run mode (All, Server)
  • fieldManager: string - Name of the manager associated with this operation
  • pretty: string - Pretty-print the output
Return Value
  • 201 (ClusterRoleBinding): Created - ClusterRoleBinding created successfully
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required
  • 409: Conflict - ClusterRoleBinding with same name already exists
5 Practical Django Examples

update - Replace the specified ClusterRoleBinding

HTTP Request: PUT /apis/rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1/clusterrolebindings/{name} | kubectl: kubectl replace -f clusterrolebinding.yaml
Full Description

The update operation replaces an existing ClusterRoleBinding with a new configuration. This is useful when you need to change the subjects bound to a ClusterRole or modify the ClusterRole reference in your anihpj Django application. Unlike patch operations, update replaces the entire resource, so you must provide the complete ClusterRoleBinding specification including unchanged fields.

Syntax
# Replace ClusterRoleBinding from YAML file
kubectl replace -f clusterrolebinding.yaml
# Apply updated configuration
kubectl apply -f clusterrolebinding.yaml
Parameters Description
  • name: string, required - Name of the ClusterRoleBinding to replace
  • body: ClusterRoleBinding, required - Complete ClusterRoleBinding object
  • dryRun: string - Dry run mode (All, Server)
  • fieldManager: string - Name of the manager associated with this operation
Return Value
  • 200 (ClusterRoleBinding): OK - ClusterRoleBinding updated successfully
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required
  • 404: Not Found - ClusterRoleBinding does not exist

patch - Partially update the specified ClusterRoleBinding

HTTP Request: PATCH /apis/rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1/clusterrolebindings/{name} | kubectl: kubectl patch clusterrolebinding {name}
Full Description

The patch operation allows you to partially update a ClusterRoleBinding without replacing the entire resource. This is useful for making targeted changes like adding labels, updating annotations, or modifying specific subjects in your anihpj Django application's ClusterRoleBindings. You can use strategic merge patches, JSON merge patches, or JSON patches depending on your needs.

Syntax
# Strategic merge patch
kubectl patch clusterrolebinding {name} -p '{"metadata":{"labels":{"new-label":"value"}}}'
# JSON merge patch
kubectl patch clusterrolebinding {name} --type=merge -p '{"metadata":{"annotations":{"key":"value"}}}'
# JSON patch
kubectl patch clusterrolebinding {name} --type=json -p='[{"op": "add", "path": "/metadata/labels/env", "value": "prod"}]'
Parameters Description
  • name: string, required - Name of the ClusterRoleBinding to patch
  • body: Patch, required - Patch object containing the changes
  • dryRun: string - Dry run mode (All, Server)
  • fieldManager: string - Name of the manager associated with this operation
  • force: boolean - Force apply the patch
Return Value
  • 200 (ClusterRoleBinding): OK - ClusterRoleBinding patched successfully
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required
  • 404: Not Found - ClusterRoleBinding does not exist
5 Practical Django Examples
Example 1: Patch Skills Service ClusterRoleBinding to Add Label

Add environment label to Skills ClusterRoleBinding using strategic merge patch.

# Add environment label to Skills ClusterRoleBinding
kubectl patch clusterrolebinding anihpj-skills-configmap-reader \
  -p '{"metadata":{"labels":{"environment":"production"}}}'
clusterrolebinding.rbac.authorization.k8s.io/anihpj-skills-configmap-reader patched
Example 2: Patch User Service ClusterRoleBinding with Annotation

Add descriptive annotation to User ClusterRoleBinding using merge patch.

# Add annotation to User ClusterRoleBinding
kubectl patch clusterrolebinding anihpj-user-deployment-manager \
  --type=merge \
  -p '{"metadata":{"annotations":{"description":"User service deployment management permissions"}}}'
clusterrolebinding.rbac.authorization.k8s.io/anihpj-user-deployment-manager patched
Example 3: Patch Author Service ClusterRoleBinding using JSON Patch

Add version label to Author ClusterRoleBinding using JSON patch operation.

# Add version label using JSON patch
kubectl patch clusterrolebinding anihpj-author-multi-access \
  --type=json \
  -p='[{"op": "add", "path": "/metadata/labels/version", "value": "v1.2"}]'
clusterrolebinding.rbac.authorization.k8s.io/anihpj-author-multi-access patched
Example 4: Patch Location Service ClusterRoleBinding Multiple Labels

Example 5: Patch JobPost Service ClusterRoleBinding from File

delete - Delete a ClusterRoleBinding

HTTP Request: DELETE /apis/rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1/clusterrolebindings/{name} | kubectl: kubectl delete clusterrolebinding {name}
Full Description

The delete operation removes a ClusterRoleBinding from your Kubernetes cluster, immediately revoking the cluster-wide permissions granted to the bound subjects. This is critical for security management in your anihpj Django application when service accounts no longer need specific permissions or when decommissioning services. Always verify the impact before deleting ClusterRoleBindings as it can immediately affect running services.

Syntax
# Delete specific ClusterRoleBinding
kubectl delete clusterrolebinding {name}
# Delete with confirmation
kubectl delete clusterrolebinding {name} --wait=true
# Delete from file
kubectl delete -f clusterrolebinding.yaml
Parameters Description
  • name: string, required - Name of the ClusterRoleBinding to delete
  • gracePeriodSeconds: integer - Duration in seconds before forcefully terminating
  • propagationPolicy: string - How to handle dependent objects (Foreground, Background, Orphan)
  • dryRun: string - Dry run mode (All, Server)
Return Value
  • 200 (Status): OK - ClusterRoleBinding deleted successfully
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required
  • 404: Not Found - ClusterRoleBinding does not exist
5 Practical Django Examples
Example 1: Delete Skills Service Development ClusterRoleBinding

Remove development ClusterRoleBinding for Skills service when moving to production.

deletecollection - Delete collection of ClusterRoleBinding

HTTP Request: DELETE /apis/rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1/clusterrolebindings | kubectl: kubectl delete clusterrolebindings --selector={selector}
Full Description

The deletecollection operation removes multiple ClusterRoleBindings based on label selectors or field selectors in a single API call. This is extremely powerful for bulk cleanup operations in your anihpj Django application, such as removing all ClusterRoleBindings for a specific environment or model. Use this operation carefully as it can revoke permissions for multiple services simultaneously, potentially affecting cluster operations.

Syntax
# Delete collection by label selector
kubectl delete clusterrolebindings -l environment=staging
# Delete collection by multiple labels
kubectl delete clusterrolebindings -l app=anihpj,tier=test
# Delete all ClusterRoleBindings (dangerous!)
kubectl delete clusterrolebindings --all
Parameters Description
  • labelSelector: string - Selector to restrict deletion by labels
  • fieldSelector: string - Selector to restrict deletion by fields
  • gracePeriodSeconds: integer - Duration before forcefully terminating
  • propagationPolicy: string - How to handle dependent objects
  • dryRun: string - Dry run mode (All, Server)
Return Value
  • 200 (Status): OK - Collection deleted successfully
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required
5 Practical Django Examples

📜 Policy Resources

Policy resources for managing API priority and fairness in Kubernetes

FlowSchema

FlowSchema Overview

FlowSchemaSpec - Specification of FlowSchema
FlowSchemaStatus - Current status of FlowSchema
FlowSchemaList - Collection of FlowSchemas
Operations - API operations for management
Official Docs: FlowSchema v1 API | API Version: flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1

FlowSchema defines the schema of a group of flows.

Full Description

FlowSchema defines the schema of a group of flows, enabling fine-grained control over API priority and fairness in Kubernetes. A flow is made up of a set of inbound API requests with similar attributes and is identified by a pair of strings: the name of the FlowSchema and a "flow distinguisher". This resource is essential for managing API request priorities in your anihpj Django application, ensuring that critical operations from your jobpost app components receive appropriate priority.

In production Django environments, FlowSchemas allow you to categorize and prioritize requests based on the subject making the request (ServiceAccounts, Users, Groups) and the resources being accessed. For example, you can give high priority to Skills model updates while assigning lower priority to bulk JobPost queries. This ensures your User authentication services maintain responsiveness even under heavy load from Author content creation or Location geocoding operations.

Syntax

# Create a FlowSchema from YAML file
kubectl create -f flowschema.yaml
# Apply a FlowSchema configuration
kubectl apply -f flowschema.yaml
# List all FlowSchemas
kubectl get flowschemas
# Get detailed information about a specific FlowSchema
kubectl describe flowschema {name}
# Get FlowSchema in YAML format
kubectl get flowschema {name} -o yaml
# Get FlowSchema in JSON format
kubectl get flowschema {name} -o json
# Delete a specific FlowSchema
kubectl delete flowschema {name}

YAML Structure

apiVersion: flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1
kind: FlowSchema
metadata:
  name: anihpj-flow
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: api-priority
spec:
  distinguisherMethod:
    type: ByUser
  matchingPrecedence: 500
  priorityLevelConfiguration:
    name: workload-high
  rules:
  - subjects:
    - kind: ServiceAccount
      serviceAccount:
        name: anihpj-skills-sa
        namespace: default
    resourceRules:
    - apiGroups: [""]
      resources: ["pods", "configmaps"]
      verbs: ["get", "list", "watch"]
status:
  conditions:
  - type: Ready
    status: "True"
    lastTransitionTime: "2025-11-10T10:00:00Z"
    reason: FlowSchemaInEffect
    message: This FlowSchema is in effect

Parameters Description

  • apiVersion: string - API version, always "flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1" for FlowSchema
  • kind: string - Resource type, always "FlowSchema"
  • metadata: ObjectMeta - Standard object metadata including name, labels, and annotations for organizing FlowSchemas in your anihpj application
  • spec: FlowSchemaSpec - Specification of the desired behavior of the FlowSchema
    • distinguisherMethod: FlowDistinguisherMethod - Defines how to compute the flow distinguisher for requests matching this schema
    • matchingPrecedence: integer - Used to choose among FlowSchemas that match a request. Lower values have higher priority. Range: 1-10000
    • priorityLevelConfiguration: PriorityLevelConfigurationReference - References the PriorityLevelConfiguration that applies to this FlowSchema
    • rules: []PolicyRulesWithSubjects - Describes which requests will match this FlowSchema based on subjects and resources
  • status: FlowSchemaStatus - Current status of the FlowSchema, including conditions indicating whether it's in effect

Return Value

  • 200 (FlowSchema): OK - Request successful, FlowSchema returned
  • 201 (FlowSchema): Created - FlowSchema successfully created
  • 202 (FlowSchema): Accepted - Request accepted for processing
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: FlowSchema for Skills Service Requests

This example creates a FlowSchema prioritizing requests from the Skills service account.

# Create FlowSchema for Skills requests
cat <<EOF | kubectl apply -f -
apiVersion: flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1
kind: FlowSchema
metadata:
  name: skills-service-flow
spec:
  distinguisherMethod:
    type: ByUser
  matchingPrecedence: 500
  priorityLevelConfiguration:
    name: workload-high
  rules:
  - subjects:
    - kind: ServiceAccount
      serviceAccount:
        name: skills-service-account
        namespace: anihpj
    resourceRules:
    - apiGroups: [""]
      resources: ["configmaps", "secrets"]
      verbs: ["get", "list", "watch"]
EOF
flowschema.flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/skills-service-flow created
Example 2: FlowSchema for User Management API

This example creates a FlowSchema for User model API requests.

# Create FlowSchema for User API
cat <<EOF | kubectl apply -f -
apiVersion: flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1
kind: FlowSchema
metadata:
  name: user-api-flow
spec:
  distinguisherMethod:
    type: ByNamespace
  matchingPrecedence: 800
  priorityLevelConfiguration:
    name: workload-low
  rules:
  - subjects:
    - kind: Group
      group:
        name: system:serviceaccounts:anihpj
    resourceRules:
    - apiGroups: ["apps"]
      resources: ["deployments"]
      namespaces: ["anihpj"]
      verbs: ["get", "list", "watch"]
EOF
flowschema.flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/user-api-flow created
Example 3: FlowSchema for Author Publishing Workflow

This example creates a FlowSchema for Author content publishing operations.

# Create FlowSchema for Author publishing
cat <<EOF | kubectl apply -f -
apiVersion: flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1
kind: FlowSchema
metadata:
  name: author-publish-flow
spec:
  distinguisherMethod:
    type: ByUser
  matchingPrecedence: 300
  priorityLevelConfiguration:
    name: workload-high
  rules:
  - subjects:
    - kind: ServiceAccount
      serviceAccount:
        name: author-publisher
        namespace: anihpj

    - apiGroups: ["batch"]

    - apiGroups: [""]
      resources: ["pods"]
      verbs: ["get", "list", "watch"]
EOF

Example 4: FlowSchema for Location Service Discovery

This example creates a FlowSchema for Location service discovery requests.

# Create FlowSchema for Location discovery
kubectl create -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1
kind: FlowSchema
metadata:
  name: location-discovery-flow
  labels:
    app: location
    model: location
spec:
  distinguisherMethod:
    type: ByUser
  matchingPrecedence: 1000
  priorityLevelConfiguration:
    name: exempt
  rules:
  - subjects:
    - kind: ServiceAccount
      serviceAccount:
        name: location-service
        namespace: anihpj
    nonResourceRules:
    - nonResourceURLs: ["/api/v1/locations/*"]
      verbs: ["get"]
EOF
flowschema.flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/location-discovery-flow created
Example 5: FlowSchema for JobPost Batch Processing

This example creates a FlowSchema for JobPost batch job processing with high priority.

# Create FlowSchema for JobPost batch jobs
cat <<EOF | kubectl apply -f -
apiVersion: flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1
kind: FlowSchema
metadata:
  name: jobpost-batch-flow
  annotations:
    description: "Priority flow for JobPost batch processing"
spec:
  distinguisherMethod:
    type: ByUser
  matchingPrecedence: 200
  priorityLevelConfiguration:
    name: workload-high
  rules:
  - subjects:
    - kind: ServiceAccount
      serviceAccount:
        name: jobpost-batch-processor
        namespace: anihpj
    resourceRules:
    - apiGroups: ["batch"]
      resources: ["jobs", "cronjobs"]
      verbs: ["create", "update", "patch", "delete"]
    - apiGroups: [""]
      resources: ["pods", "pods/log"]
      verbs: ["get", "list", "watch"]
EOF
flowschema.flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/jobpost-batch-flow created

FlowSchemaSpec

Full Description

FlowSchemaSpec describes how the FlowSchema's specification looks like, defining the matching rules and priority configuration for API request flows. In your anihpj Django application, this specification determines how requests from different services (Skills, User, Author, Location, JobPost) are categorized and prioritized.

The spec includes the distinguisher method (how to group similar requests), matching precedence (priority order), priority level configuration reference, and matching rules based on subjects and resources. This allows fine-grained control over which requests from your jobpost app components receive higher or lower priority in the cluster.

Syntax

# View FlowSchemaSpec in a FlowSchema
kubectl get flowschema {name} -o jsonpath='{.spec}'
# View FlowSchemaSpec in YAML format
kubectl get flowschema {name} -o yaml | grep -A 20 "spec:"
# Describe FlowSchema to see spec details
kubectl describe flowschema {name}

Parameters Description

  • distinguisherMethod (FlowDistinguisherMethod): defines how to compute the flow distinguisher for requests that match this schema
    • type (string), required: type of flow distinguisher method. Supported types are "ByUser" and "ByNamespace"
  • matchingPrecedence (int32): used to choose among the FlowSchemas that match a given request. Values must be ranged in [1,10000]. Default: 1000
  • priorityLevelConfiguration (PriorityLevelConfigurationReference), required: should reference a PriorityLevelConfiguration in the cluster
    • name (string), required: name of the priority level configuration being referenced
  • rules ([]PolicyRulesWithSubjects): describes which requests will match this flow schema
    • subjects ([]Subject), required: list of normal user, serviceaccount, or group
    • resourceRules ([]ResourcePolicyRule): slice of ResourcePolicyRules
    • nonResourceRules ([]NonResourcePolicyRule): list of NonResourcePolicyRules

Return Value

  • FlowSchemaSpec object: Returns the specification portion of a FlowSchema

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: FlowSchemaSpec for Skills Service

This example shows a FlowSchemaSpec prioritizing Skills model requests.

spec:
  distinguisherMethod:
    type: ByUser
  matchingPrecedence: 500
  priorityLevelConfiguration:
    name: workload-high
  rules:
  - subjects:
    - kind: ServiceAccount
      serviceAccount:
        name: anihpj-skills-sa
        namespace: default
    resourceRules:
    - apiGroups: [""]
      resources: ["configmaps"]
      verbs: ["get", "list"]
# View the spec
kubectl get flowschema skills-flow -o jsonpath='{.spec}' | jq
{"distinguisherMethod":{"type":"ByUser"},"matchingPrecedence":500,"priorityLevelConfiguration":{"name":"workload-high"},"rules":[{"resourceRules":[{"apiGroups":[""],"resources":["configmaps"],"verbs":["get","list"]}],"subjects":[{"kind":"ServiceAccount","serviceAccount":{"name":"anihpj-skills-sa","namespace":"default"}}]}]}
Example 2: FlowSchemaSpec for User Authentication

This example demonstrates a FlowSchemaSpec for User model authentication flows.

spec:
  distinguisherMethod:
    type: ByNamespace
  matchingPrecedence: 300
  priorityLevelConfiguration:
    name: workload-high
  rules:
  - subjects:
    - kind: ServiceAccount
      serviceAccount:
        name: anihpj-user-sa
        namespace: default
    resourceRules:
    - apiGroups: [""]
      resources: ["secrets"]
      verbs: ["get"]
# Describe to see spec details
kubectl describe flowschema user-auth-flow
Name: user-auth-flow API Version: flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1 Kind: FlowSchema Spec: Distinguisher Method: Type: ByNamespace Matching Precedence: 300 Priority Level Configuration: Name: workload-high Rules: Resource Rules: API Groups: Resources: secrets Verbs: get
Example 3: FlowSchemaSpec for Author Publishing

This example illustrates a FlowSchemaSpec for Author content publishing operations.

  distinguisherMethod:
    type: ByUser
  matchingPrecedence: 400
  priorityLevelConfiguration:
    name: workload-medium
  rules:
  - subjects:
    - kind: Group
      group:
        name: system:serviceaccounts:anihpj
    resourceRules:
    - apiGroups: ["apps"]
      resources: ["deployments"]
      verbs: ["update", "patch"]
# Get spec in YAML format
kubectl get flowschema author-publish-flow -o yaml | grep -A 15 "spec:"
spec: distinguisherMethod: type: ByUser matchingPrecedence: 400 priorityLevelConfiguration: name: workload-medium rules: - resourceRules: - apiGroups: - apps resources: - deployments verbs: - update - patch
Example 4: FlowSchemaSpec for Location Geocoding

This example shows a FlowSchemaSpec for Location model geocoding services.

This example demonstrates a FlowSchemaSpec for JobPost model bulk query operations.

FlowSchemaStatus

Full Description

FlowSchemaStatus represents the current state of a FlowSchema, providing runtime information about whether the flow schema is active and being enforced by the API server. In your anihpj Django application, monitoring the status helps ensure your priority configurations for Skills, User, Author, Location, and JobPost services are properly applied.

The status includes a conditions array that tracks the FlowSchema's operational state. The primary condition type is "Dangling" which indicates whether the referenced PriorityLevelConfiguration exists. A healthy FlowSchema will show conditions confirming it's in effect and properly configured for your jobpost app's API priority management.

Syntax

# View FlowSchemaStatus
kubectl get flowschema {name} -o jsonpath='{.status}'
# View status conditions
kubectl get flowschema {name} -o jsonpath='{.status.conditions[*]}'
# Check if FlowSchema is active
kubectl describe flowschema {name} | grep -A 5 "Status:"

Parameters Description

  • conditions ([]FlowSchemaCondition): list of the current states of FlowSchema
    • type (string): type of the condition
    • status (string): status of the condition. Can be True, False, Unknown
    • lastTransitionTime (Time): last time the condition transitioned from one status to another
    • reason (string): unique, one-word, CamelCase reason for the condition's last transition
    • message (string): human-readable message indicating details about last transition

Return Value

  • FlowSchemaStatus object: Returns the status portion of a FlowSchema with current conditions

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Check Skills Service FlowSchema Status

This example shows how to verify the status of a Skills service FlowSchema.

# Get FlowSchema status
kubectl get flowschema skills-flow -o jsonpath='{.status}' | jq
{"conditions":[{"lastTransitionTime":"2025-11-10T10:00:00Z","message":"This FlowSchema is in effect","reason":"FlowSchemaInEffect","status":"True","type":"Ready"}]}
Example 2: Monitor User Authentication FlowSchema Conditions

This example demonstrates checking the conditions array for User model FlowSchema.

# View all status conditions
kubectl get flowschema user-auth-flow -o jsonpath='{.status.conditions[*]}' | jq
{"lastTransitionTime":"2025-11-10T09:30:00Z","message":"This FlowSchema references the PriorityLevelConfiguration object named 'workload-high' and it exists","reason":"NotDangling","status":"False","type":"Dangling"}
Example 3: Verify Author Publishing FlowSchema Is Active

This example illustrates how to confirm an Author service FlowSchema is properly configured.

# Describe to see full status
kubectl describe flowschema author-publish-flow | grep -A 10 "Status:"
Status: Conditions: Last Transition Time: 2025-11-10T08:45:00Z Message: This FlowSchema is in effect Reason: FlowSchemaInEffect Status: True Type: Ready Last Transition Time: 2025-11-10T08:45:00Z Message: This FlowSchema references the PriorityLevelConfiguration object named 'workload-medium' and it exists Reason: NotDangling Status: False
Example 4: Check Location Geocoding FlowSchema Transition Time

This example shows how to extract the last transition time from FlowSchema status.

# Get last transition time
kubectl get flowschema location-geocode-flow -o jsonpath='{.status.conditions[0].lastTransitionTime}'
2025-11-10T07:20:00Z
Example 5: Verify JobPost Queries FlowSchema Health

This example demonstrates checking if a JobPost FlowSchema's referenced PriorityLevel exists.

# Check for Dangling condition
kubectl get flowschema jobpost-queries-flow -o jsonpath='{.status.conditions[?(@.type=="Dangling")].status}'
False

FlowSchemaList

FlowSchemaList is a list of FlowSchema objects

YAML Structure

apiVersion: flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1
kind: FlowSchemaList
metadata: ListMeta
items: []FlowSchema

Parameters Description

  • apiVersion: string - API version, always "flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1" for FlowSchemaList
  • kind: string - Resource type, always "FlowSchemaList"
  • metadata (ListMeta): Standard list metadata including resourceVersion and continue token for pagination
  • items ([]FlowSchema), required: List of FlowSchema objects in the collection

Return Value

  • 200 (FlowSchemaList): OK - Request successful, FlowSchemaList returned
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: List All FlowSchemas

This example lists all FlowSchemas in the cluster.

# List all FlowSchemas

This example lists FlowSchemas with additional details.

Example 3: Get FlowSchemas in YAML Format

FlowSchema Operations

Operations Overview

get - Read the specified FlowSchema
get status - Read status of the specified FlowSchema
list - List FlowSchemas
create - Create a FlowSchema
update - Replace the specified FlowSchema
update status - Replace status of the specified FlowSchema
patch - Partially update the specified FlowSchema
patch status - Partially update status of the specified FlowSchema
delete - Delete a FlowSchema
deletecollection - Delete collection of FlowSchema

Operations allow you to interact with FlowSchema resources through the Kubernetes API. These operations enable you to manage API priority and fairness configurations for your anihpj Django application, ensuring optimal request handling for Skills, User, Author, Location, and JobPost services.

get - read the specified FlowSchema

Read details of a specific FlowSchema by name.

HTTP Request
GET /apis/flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1/flowschemas/{name}
Parameters
  • name (in path): string, required - name of the FlowSchema
  • pretty (in query): string - pretty print output
Return Value
  • 200 (FlowSchema): OK
  • 401: Unauthorized
5 Practical Django Examples

create - create a FlowSchema

HTTP Request
POST /apis/flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1/flowschemas
Parameters
  • body: FlowSchema, required - FlowSchema to create
  • dryRun (in query): string - dryRun
  • fieldManager (in query): string - fieldManager
  • fieldValidation (in query): string - fieldValidation
  • pretty (in query): string - pretty
Return Value
  • 200 (FlowSchema): OK
  • 201 (FlowSchema): Created
  • 202 (FlowSchema): Accepted
  • 401: Unauthorized
5 Practical Django Examples
Example 1: Create Skills Analytics FlowSchema

This example creates a FlowSchema for Skills model analytics queries.

# Create FlowSchema for analytics
cat <<EOF | kubectl create -f -
apiVersion: flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1
kind: FlowSchema
metadata:
  name: skills-analytics-flow
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    model: skills
    component: analytics
spec:
  distinguisherMethod:
    type: ByUser
  matchingPrecedence: 400
  priorityLevelConfiguration:
    name: workload-low
  rules:
  - subjects:
    - kind: ServiceAccount
      serviceAccount:
        name: skills-analytics
        namespace: anihpj
    resourceRules:
    - apiGroups: [""]
      resources: ["pods", "pods/log"]
      verbs: ["get", "list"]
EOF
flowschema.flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/skills-analytics-flow created
Example 2: Create User Authentication FlowSchema

This example creates a FlowSchema for User model authentication operations.

# Create authentication FlowSchema
kubectl create -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1
kind: FlowSchema
metadata:
  name: user-auth-flow
  annotations:
    description: "User authentication priority flow"
spec:
  distinguisherMethod:
    type: ByUser
  matchingPrecedence: 100
  priorityLevelConfiguration:
    name: exempt
  rules:
  - subjects:
    - kind: ServiceAccount
      serviceAccount:
        name: user-auth-service
        namespace: anihpj
    nonResourceRules:
    - nonResourceURLs: ["/api/v1/auth/*"]
      verbs: ["get", "post"]
EOF
flowschema.flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/user-auth-flow created

update - replace the specified FlowSchema

Replace the entire FlowSchema configuration with a new specification.

HTTP Request
PUT /apis/flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1/flowschemas/{name}
Parameters
  • name (in path): string, required - name of the FlowSchema
  • body: FlowSchema, required - Updated FlowSchema object
  • dryRun (in query): string - dryRun
  • fieldManager (in query): string - fieldManager
  • fieldValidation (in query): string - fieldValidation
  • pretty (in query): string - pretty
Return Value
  • 200 (FlowSchema): OK
  • 201 (FlowSchema): Created
  • 401: Unauthorized
Practical Django Examples
Example 1: Update Skills FlowSchema Precedence

This example updates the matching precedence for the Skills service FlowSchema.

# Get current FlowSchema, modify, and update
kubectl get flowschema skills-service-flow -o yaml > skills-flow.yaml
# Edit the file to change matchingPrecedence from 500 to 450
sed -i 's/matchingPrecedence: 500/matchingPrecedence: 450/' skills-flow.yaml
kubectl replace -f skills-flow.yaml
flowschema.flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/skills-service-flow replaced

  name: user-api-flow

  distinguisherMethod:
    type: ByNamespace
  matchingPrecedence: 800
  priorityLevelConfiguration:
    name: workload-high
  rules:
  - subjects:
    - kind: Group
      group:
        name: system:serviceaccounts:anihpj
    resourceRules:
    - apiGroups: ["apps"]
      resources: ["deployments"]
      namespaces: ["anihpj"]
      verbs: ["get", "list", "watch", "update"]

This example changes the distinguisher method for Location discovery FlowSchema.

# Change distinguisher method
cat <<EOF | kubectl replace -f -
apiVersion: flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/v1
kind: FlowSchema
metadata:
  name: location-discovery-flow
  labels:
    app: location
    model: location
spec:
  distinguisherMethod:
    type: ByNamespace
  matchingPrecedence: 1000
  priorityLevelConfiguration:
    name: exempt
  rules:
  - subjects:
    - kind: Group
      group:
        name: system:serviceaccounts:anihpj
    nonResourceRules:
    - nonResourceURLs: ["/api/v1/locations/*"]
      verbs: ["get"]
EOF
flowschema.flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/location-discovery-flow replaced
Example 5: Update JobPost FlowSchema with Additional Subjects

This example adds user subjects to the JobPost batch processing FlowSchema.

# Add user subjects
kubectl get flowschema jobpost-batch-flow -o yaml > jobpost-flow.yaml
cat <<EOF >> jobpost-flow-patch.yaml
spec:
  rules:
  - subjects:
    - kind: ServiceAccount
      serviceAccount:
        name: jobpost-batch-processor
        namespace: anihpj
    - kind: User
      user:
        name: batch-admin@anihpj.com
EOF
kubectl replace -f jobpost-flow.yaml
flowschema.flowcontrol.apiserver.k8s.io/jobpost-batch-flow replaced

Role Overview

RoleList - Collection of Roles
Operations - API operations for management
Official Docs: Role v1 API | API Version: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1

Role is a namespaced, logical grouping of PolicyRules that can be referenced as a unit by a RoleBinding.

Full Description

Role provides namespace-scoped access control for your anihpj Django application, enabling fine-grained permissions within specific namespaces. Each Role in your jobpost application defines what actions can be performed on cluster resources, making it essential for securing your Skills, Author, Location, and JobPost services.

By creating dedicated Roles, you can follow the principle of least privilege, ensuring that each service only has access to the resources it needs. For example, your Skills service might need a Role that allows reading ConfigMaps and creating Pods, while your JobPost service requires a Role with broader permissions for managing Deployments and Services within its namespace.

Syntax

# Create a Role from YAML file
kubectl create -f role.yaml
# Create a Role imperatively
kubectl create role {name} --verb={verb} --resource={resource} --namespace={namespace}
# List all Roles in a namespace
kubectl get roles -n {namespace}
# List all Roles (short form)
kubectl get roles
# Get detailed information about a specific Role
kubectl describe role {name} -n {namespace}
# Get Role in YAML format
kubectl get role {name} -n {namespace} -o yaml
# Delete a specific Role
kubectl delete role {name} -n {namespace}

YAML Structure

apiVersion: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: Role
metadata:
  namespace: anihpj-production
  name: anihpj-jobpost-manager
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    service: jobpost
    tier: backend
spec:
rules:
- apiGroups: [""]
  resources: ["pods", "configmaps", "secrets"]
  verbs: ["get", "list", "watch", "create", "update", "patch", "delete"]
- apiGroups: ["apps"]
  resources: ["deployments", "replicasets"]
  verbs: ["get", "list", "watch", "create", "update", "patch", "delete"]
- apiGroups: [""]
  resources: ["services"]
  verbs: ["get", "list", "watch"]

Parameters Description

  • metadata (ObjectMeta): Standard object's metadata
  • rules ([]PolicyRule): Rules holds all the PolicyRules for this Role (atomic: will be replaced during a merge)
  • rules.apiGroups ([]string): APIGroups containing the resources ("" for core, "*" for all)
  • rules.resources ([]string): List of resources this rule applies to ("*" for all)
  • rules.verbs ([]string), required: List of verbs that apply to ALL ResourceKinds ("*" for all)
  • rules.resourceNames ([]string): Optional white list of names (empty means everything allowed)
  • rules.nonResourceURLs ([]string): Set of partial URLs for non-resource access

Return Value

  • 200 (Role): OK - Request successful, Role returned
  • 201 (Role): Created - Role successfully created
  • 202 (Role): Accepted - Request accepted for processing
  • 401: Unauthorized - Authentication required

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Skills Service Manager Role

This example demonstrates creating a dedicated Role for the Skills model service in the jobpost app.

apiVersion: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: Role
metadata:
  namespace: anihpj-production
  name: anihpj-skills-manager
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    service: skills
    model: Skills
spec:
rules:
- apiGroups: [""]
  resources: ["pods", "configmaps", "secrets"]
  verbs: ["get", "list", "watch", "create", "update", "patch", "delete"]
- apiGroups: ["apps"]
  resources: ["deployments"]
  verbs: ["get", "list", "watch", "update", "patch"]
# Create Role for Skills service
kubectl create -f skills-manager-role.yaml
# Verify the Role was created
kubectl get role anihpj-skills-manager -n anihpj-production
role.rbac.authorization.k8s.io/anihpj-skills-manager created NAME CREATED AT anihpj-skills-manager 2024-11-10T10:30:45Z
Example 2: User Service Reader Role

This example shows creating a read-only Role for User model authentication service.

  namespace: anihpj-shared

  labels:
    app: anihpj
    service: user
    model: User
    permission: readonly
spec:

- apiGroups: [""]
  resources: ["configmaps", "secrets"]
  verbs: ["get", "list", "watch"]
- apiGroups: [""]
  resources: ["services", "endpoints"]
  verbs: ["get", "list"]

Example 5: JobPost Service Multi-API Group Role

This example demonstrates creating a Role for the JobPost model spanning multiple API groups.

apiVersion: rbac.authorization.k8s.io/v1
kind: Role

  namespace: anihpj-jobs

  labels:
    app: anihpj

    model: JobPost
    scope: multi-api

- apiGroups: ["", "apps", "extensions"]
  resources: ["pods", "deployments", "services", "configmaps"]
  verbs: ["get", "list", "watch"]
- apiGroups: ["batch"]
  resources: ["jobs", "cronjobs"]
  verbs: ["get", "list", "watch", "create", "update", "patch", "delete"]
- apiGroups: ["autoscaling"]
  resources: ["horizontalpodautoscalers"]
  verbs: ["get", "list", "create", "update"]
# Create multi-API Role for JobPost service
